Galleries\nVideos\nMENU\nBreadcrumb\nHome\nTechnology\nFebruary 14, 2017 11:00 PM\nAfter controversy, LinkNYC finds its niche\nGerald Schifman\nTweet\nShare\nShare\nEmail\nMore\nPrint\nPeter D'Amato\nThe number of people using Wi-Fi through the kiosks has surged.\nAfter some early controversy, the LinkNYC project is gaining a foothold. The installation of Wi-Fi kiosks across the city\xe2\x80\x94582 and counting\xe2\x80\x94has attracted more and more users during the past few months.\nA comparison of typical periods from last month and September reflects the change. Wi-Fi sessions on LinkNYC kiosks were 51% higher during the week of Jan. 9 than during the week of Sept. 26. Over that time frame, New Yorkers logged more than 5.4 million hours on the free Wi-Fi.\nThe Links kiosks, which replaced pay phones scattered throughout the city, provide free Wi-Fi, phone calls and USB charging. Originally internet browsing services were available via each kiosk's built-in tablet. The internet service proved to be problematic, though, as people complained that homeless and other users were monopolizing the kiosks, often using the tablets to view pornography. The tablets were disabled in mid-September, and the kiosks received a software update.\nSince the reboot, the number of people using the Wi-Fi has surged, although the figures are not comparable to earlier data. A LinkNYC spokeswoman said the improved numbers reflect more accurate usage statistics following the software update. The number of sessions per week has increased since the software tweak.\nThe kiosks are making an economic impact on the city. LinkNYC's owner, CityBridge\xe2\x80\x94a consortium of four firms including Qualcomm\xe2\x80\x94estimates that the program created 350 direct full-time jobs last year, plus 265 jobs coming via multiplier effects. Those 615 workers took home $68.4 million in income, creating $128.9 million in economic output\xe2\x80\x94a 74% increase from 2015. It's a small portion of the city's more than $1 trillion in annual economic activity, but LinkNYC is growing and providing access to the internet for some who might not otherwise get it.\nRelated Articles\nTech industry joins lawsuit against Muslim ban\nNY tech takes next step in anti-Trump campaign\n&lt;em&gt;New York Times&lt;/em&gt; bundles Spotify service with digital subscr\xe2\x80\xa6\nIf New York software engineers make so much money, why are they at the bottom o\xe2\x80\xa6\nVerizon could get a $250 million discount on Yahoo after hacks\nSpotify finalizes deal for 4 World Trade Center space\nABC sells out ad time for the Oscars\nNew York to require banks and insurers to step up cybersecurity\nYahoo salvages Verizon deal with $350 million discount\nGet rid of those Wi-Fi kiosks\nView the discussion thread.\nGet our newsletters\nStaying current is easy with Crain's New York news delivered straight to your inbox, free of charge\nEmail Address\nCrain's Student Offer\nWe offer a discounted rate through Student Beans for students with a valid .edu email address. Island\nTransit\nSports\nOpinion\nJim Marguiles\nCartoon roundup\nWeather\n79\xc2\xb0\n6/23/2019\nGood Afternoon\nNews\nLinkNYC continues rapid public Wi-Fi expansion in Brooklyn, Queens\nWashington Heights resident Anthony Ramos charges his mobile phone at a\nLinkNYC kiosk on Third Avenue at East 43rd Street in Manhattan on Wednesday, March 29, 2017. LinkNYC kiosks are replacing almost all of\nNew York City's 6,000 remaining pay phones.\nPhoto Credit: Charles Eckert\nBy Ivan Pereira and Laura Figueroa ivan.pereira@amny.com, laura.figueroa@newsday.com\n@IvanPer4\nMarch 29, 2017 8:30 PM\nPrint\nShare\nfbShare\nTweet\nEmail\nAn influx of outerboro communities will be linked in this year.\nThe city is on track to meet the 7,500 installation benchmark of its public kiosks, LinkNYC, by 2023 and the majority of the 150 confirmed to go online this spring and summer are in Brooklyn and Queens neighborhoods including Astoria, Park Slope, Long Island City and Flatbush, according to the city\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Information Technology and Telecommunication (DoITT).\nThe addition comes as a relief to city leaders and residents who have called for more equity in distribution of the new technology, which offers\xc2\xa0free phone service, WiFi, charging ports and has been replacing traditional payphones since its launch last year.\nrecommended reading\nCity: LinkNYC kiosks surpass 1 million users\nThey\xe2\x80\x99re excited for the expansion even though the service has been at times beset by controversies ranging from the kiosks being monopolized by individuals looking at pornography and privacy concerns related to user data.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think to date there\xe2\x80\x99s been a concentration in Manhattan, and I\xe2\x80\x99ve said we have to get the outer boroughs equally served, that is the aim,\xe2\x80\x9d said Bronx City Councilman James Vacca, the chair of the Council\xe2\x80\x99s Committee on Technology, after receiving an update on LinkNYC Wednesday.\nThere have been roughly 150 new kiosks recently installed throughout the city, and they will be activated in the near future, according to CityBridge, the consortium behind the hot spots.\nAs of Wednesday, 667 Links were up and running in all five boroughs, the operator said.\nGet Breaking News emails\nThe latest about your city, as it happens.\nSign up\nBy clicking Sign up, you agree to our privacy policy.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have helped more than 1.3 million New Yorkers and visitors get online at the fastest speeds available in New York City, for free,\xe2\x80\x9d Jen Hensley, LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s general manager, said in a statement.\nThe kiosks initially launched with a tablet that allowed users to browse the internet, but that capability has since been turned off due to complaints from residents. Now, visitors must have their own devices to access the free WiFi.\nLinkNYC has generated $37.3 million in advertising revenue since they launched and they\xe2\x80\x99re expected to generate $25 million in the upcoming year, according to DoITT Commissioner Anne M. Roest, who testified at Wednesday\xe2\x80\x99s hearing.\nrecommended reading\nOfficial: Porn viewers are hogging free web kiosks\nVacca is optimistic that the service will straighten itself out after a first-year rife with difficulties.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re not going back,\xe2\x80\x9d Vacca said after the hearing. \xe2\x80\x9cWe learned from the experience when the city initially rolled it out.\xe2\x80\x9d\nSome New Yorkers and civil rights groups such as the NYCLU expressed concern over users\xe2\x80\x99 data mining and privacy issues. Two weeks ago, CityBridge updated its privacy policy and sought to ensure users that the kiosks don\xe2\x80\x99t store or share personal information.\nLast September, the city disabled the use of the stations\xe2\x80\x99 web browsers after fielding a number of complaints about people monopolizing the kiosks and spending hours surfing the internet, often for inappropriate material.\nIrene Meisel, a member of the group RethinkLinkNYC who attended the City Council hearing, argued that the kiosks do not go far enough to achieve their primary goal, as stated by city officials: to close the \xe2\x80\x9cdigital divide\xe2\x80\x9d faced by low-income New Yorkers without web access at home.\nMeisel said her group would like to see the city direct some of the LinkNYC revenue to programs that increase digital access to underserved communities.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe city has said that the Links were put up to address the digital divide. As they\xe2\x80\x99re currently configured now we don\xe2\x80\x99t see that they\xe2\x80\x99re doing that,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\nAbout 150 new LinkNYC kiosks will go online in the coming months. Here is where you can find them.Queens: Astoria, Long Island City, Rego Park, Elmhurst, Sunnyside, Forest Hills.Brooklyn: Flatbush, Ditmas Park, Park Slope, Greenwood, Greenpoint, Bed Stuy and Crown Heights.The Bronx: Melrose, Fordham HeightsManhattan: Harlem, Midtown\nBy Ivan Pereira and Laura Figueroa ivan.pereira@amny.com, laura.figueroa@newsday.com\n@IvanPer4\nIvan has been a staff reporter with amNewYork since May 2012 and covers breaking news, politics and enterprise stories.\nShare on Facebook\nShare on Twitter\nComments\nWe're revamping our Comments section. All rights reserved.", b"LinkNYC Kiosks Adopt Aunt Bertha Social Services App - CityLab\nSkip to content\nDesign Transportation Environment Equity Life\nLinkNYC's new Aunt Bertha app connects users with information about food pantries, emergency housing, and other social services. LinkNYC\nNew York City's Wi-Fi Kiosks Now Include a 'Yelp for Social Services'\nLaura Bliss\nApr 13, 2017\nThe move targets New Yorkers who stand to benefit most from the LinkNYC network in the first place. Share Tweet LinkedInEmailPrint\nThere\xe2\x80\x99s no blueprint for how to roll out the world\xe2\x80\x99s largest free public wi-fi network\xe2\x80\x94especially one with hundreds of web-beaming, touch-screen towers spread across five boroughs. So a little more than a year after LinkNYC installed its first kiosks around New York City, some questions are still hazy. How are they supposed to be used? Who are they really meant for?\nToday LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s purpose takes a slightly clearer shape, with the addition of Aunt Bertha, an existing app modeled as a Yelp for social safety-net services run by an Austin-based benefit corporation. LinkNYC kiosks are already equipped with access to 911 and 311, a portal to apply for government benefits, interactive maps, free phone-call capabilities, and a USB charger. Through a simple search from one of the kiosk tablets, New Yorkers can now tap into Aunt Bertha\xe2\x80\x99s robust database of food pantries, emergency housing, childcare, healthcare, transportation assistance, and financial aid programs located within that zip code.\nRecommended\nTo Court a Skeptical Public, New York Sends Wi-Fi Ambassadors\nEillie Anzilotti Aug 12, 2016\nA Portland Startup Is Smashing Barriers to Affordable Housing Laura Bliss Jan 27, 2017\nA Brazilian Vision Blooms Anew in the Bronx Amanda Kolson Hurley Jun 21, 2019\nThe app targets the New Yorkers who stand the most to gain from LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s services in the first place. A 2015 study by the city comptroller\xe2\x80\x99s office found that roughly 813,000 households (nearly 26 percent, citywide) lacked broadband access at home; 510,000 don\xe2\x80\x99t have a computer.\nThe majority of these disconnected households are surviving below the poverty line, and may benefit from the resources Aunt Bertha is designed to catalogue and serve up with ease. Founded in 2012, the platform has connected more than 280,000 people around the U.S. with services from all tiers of government, large nonprofit agencies, and neighborhood groups\xe2\x80\x94the sorts of resources otherwise buried across thousands of websites and pamphlets that can require hours or days of sifting to find.\n\xe2\x80\x9cPeople in need are almost always grappling with interrelated problems\xe2\x80\xa6 so easily accessible powerful technology tools that provide useful options in one place are key,\xe2\x80\x9d Steve Lee, a managing director at Robin Hood, a New York City anti-poverty agency, said in a statement.\nWhether New Yorkers will bite, of course, is the big-ticket question. LinkNYC has logged more than a million registered users on its wi-fi network since the kiosks first rolled out in February 2016. However, the offerings have shifted substantially: Initially, the touch-screens offered unfettered web-browsing, but that feature quickly got axed when the lure of YouTube (and porn sites) proved too disruptive to sidewalk life. And not all New Yorkers have taken enthusiastically to the 2001 Space Odyssey-like monoliths, which are owned and operated by a consortium of public and private entities with Alphabet at the center. Data privacy concerns, especially in low-income neighborhoods already experiencing disproportionate levels of police surveillance, have held plenty of users back.\nRepresentatives for LinkNYC say that the kiosks themselves don\xe2\x80\x99t require log-ins (though the wi-fi network does), and wipe any personal information entered at the end of each session. Usage data from the Aunt Bertha app, they say, will be aggregated to guide searchers to services that might be the most in-demand where they are. LinkNYC also continues to work with community groups, local libraries, youth groups, and seniors organizations to reach groups that could benefit from the services. Meanwhile, the network will continue to expand. Currently, there are a little over 800 kiosks around the city; LinkNYC expects 7,500 total by 2025.\n\xe2\x80\x9cSmart\xe2\x80\x9d technology will never solve wicked problems like urban poverty, hunger, transportation gaps, and healthcare divides on its own\xe2\x80\x94focused policies and targeted investments have to work in tandem. But if the yank-back of LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s web browsing access was a case study in unintended consequences of overly broad ambitions, a move to connect more New Yorkers with specific services is a step in a helpful direction.\nAbout the Author\nLaura Bliss\n@mslaurabliss\nFeed Laura Bliss is CityLab\xe2\x80\x99s west coast bureau chief. She also authors MapLab, a biweekly newsletter about maps (subscribe here). Her work has appeared in the New York Times, The Atlantic, Los Angeles magazine, and beyond.\nExpand Comments +\nMost Popular\nEnvironment Paris Wants to Grow \xe2\x80\x98Urban Forests\xe2\x80\x99 at Famous Landmarks The city plans to fill some small but treasured sites with trees\xe2\x80\x94a climate strategy that may also change the way Paris frames its architectural heritage.\nFeargus O'Sullivan\nJun 19, 2019\nTransportation The World's 15 Most Complex Subway Maps As ranked by a research team of mathematicians and theoretical physicists.\nEric Jaffe\nFeb 25, 2016\nDesign How Birds and Bees Survive in the City Pollinators\xe2\x80\x94the wildlife that shuffle pollen between flowers\xe2\x80\x94are being decimated. us:advertisementadvertisementadvertisement05.01.17world changing ideasA Courtroom Designed For Fairness, And Other World Changing Urban DesignsLearn about the winner of the urban design category of Fast Company\xe2\x80\x99s 2017 World Changing Ideas Awards\xe2\x80\x93and the other innovative finalists.\nBy Adele Peters8 minute ReadIt takes an average of 37 seconds for a judge in Chicago\xe2\x80\x99s Cook County to set bond: the amount of money a defendant must pay to stay out of jail before trial. When that sum is unaffordable, defendants might spend months in jail, even if they\xe2\x80\x99re accused of non-violent, low-level crimes. One man who stole toothpaste and breath mints spent\xc2\xa0308 days in jail. A pregnant woman who stole candy bars and plums spent 135 days in jail. For someone working a low-wage job, even a day or two of missed work might mean losing employment.advertisementadvertisement\xe2\x80\x9cCan physically altering a space change the narrative for a criminal justice system?\xe2\x80\x9d [Image: Cannon Design]Judges currently make these potentially life-changing rulings inside a noisy, distracting, chaotic courtroom. Designers at CannonDesign saw improving the physical environment as one step toward fairer decisions, by allowing judges to give full attention to a defendant and clearly communicate.\xe2\x80\x9cWe immediately jumped at the notion: can physically altering a space, can the inclusion of design, change the narrative for a criminal justice system that has a couple of different spotlights on it right now?\xe2\x80\x9d says Timothy Swanson, who leads the city design practice at the Chicago office of CannonDesign.\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s important for designers to work on these type of government challenges because our creative work can lead to valuable change.\xe2\x80\x9d [Image: Cannon Design]The CannonDesign team, working with the court system and the local Civic Consulting Alliance, spent the summer and part of the fall of 2016 observing bond court proceedings before coming up with a plan that improves acoustics, minimizes distracting movement, aligns parties with the judge, and features signage that clearly explains the bond ruling process to family members waiting in the corridor outside. The new courtroom, which won the urban design award in the 2017 World Changing Idea awards, is set to open this spring. (You can read about the rest of the finalists below.)\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s important for designers to work on these type of government challenges because our creative work can lead to valuable change,\xe2\x80\x9d Swanson says. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s equally important for designers to be engaged in these challenges from the outset. Often, when government agencies receive money, they need to spend it quickly and thus they may be forced to make the easiest changes in the least amount of time. However, if these agencies have engaged with designers about the challenges previously, they\xe2\x80\x99re ready with a road map to act on when they do receive funding. This is key to success.\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x9cThis can make an immediate, localized impact and it can hopefully catalyze even greater systematic improvements in the justice system.\xe2\x80\x9d [Image: Cannon Design]After the bond court redesign, the designers hope to work on other courtrooms. \xe2\x80\x9cGiven the bond court is truly the entry point for most into the judicial system, we believe there\xe2\x80\x99s also strong opportunity for this to improve fairness throughout a city\xe2\x80\x99s justice system and/or the national system\xe2\x80\x93but we\xe2\x80\x99ll need to build on it,\xe2\x80\x9d he says. \xe2\x80\x9cWe can\xe2\x80\x99t have people entering bond courts designed for equity and then advancing through the system into other courtrooms that don\xe2\x80\x99t value their dignity. So, this can make an immediate, localized impact and it can hopefully catalyze even greater systematic improvements in the justice system.\xe2\x80\x9dHere\xe2\x80\x99s more about the finalists in the urban design category:advertisementBorder CityFR-EEWhile Trump plans a border wall that could cost more than $20 billion, Mexican architect Fernando Romero proposes building a border city instead. Straddling the border between New Mexico, Texas, and the Mexican state of Chihuahua, the city would\xc2\xa0move goods and people as easily as possible rather than keeping them apart.CitySpaces MicroPADPanoramic InterestsBy building tiny, 160-square-foot apartments in a factory\xe2\x80\x93at a size that can easily fit on a standard truck, and then be stacked on site\xe2\x80\x93developers from Panoramic Interests have created a system that can be built twice as fast as a typical apartment building. The company plans to build the MicroPAD\xc2\xa0in cities like San Francisco to help provide higher-quality, less-expensive housing for the homeless. Each unit is designed with features specific to the needs of a homeless person, such as a UV light under the bed to kill bedbugs.InfarmInfarmInfarm\xe2\x80\x99s small, modular vertical farming units can be used alone\xe2\x80\x93to grow produce for a restaurant or supermarket\xe2\x80\x93or stacked in hundreds of units to create an efficient urban farm. The system uses sensors to track growing conditions, and will eventually be used to forecast demand and plan seeding schedules across a citywide network. The company is developing its first network across key hubs in Berlin in 2017.advertisementHeijmans OneHeijmansTo help provide affordable urban housing for young, single people in the Netherlands, Dutch developer Heijmans designed tiny houses that can be quickly installed on temporarily vacant lots. Designed for energy efficiency, the Heijmans One house also runs on solar power. When the lot is ready for permanent development, the house can be moved to new vacant land.Kashiwa-no-ha Smart CityZGF ArchitectsIn 2016, this development 18 miles north of Tokyo became the largest neighborhood in the world to earn a LEED Neighborhood Development Plan platinum certification. A smart grid, connected to wind and solar plants, optimizes energy use. A massive \xe2\x80\x9cplant factory\xe2\x80\x9d tests vertical farming technology. Wearables track resident health at a large scale. Research projects also focus on health, such as a model town designed to minimize chemical use.NewTown Master PlanPerkins+WillIn Brooklyn and Queens, the neighborhoods around Newtown Creek\xe2\x80\x93an infamous Superfund site\xe2\x80\x93have long been industrial. This design envisions how they could become mixed-use \xe2\x80\x9cMakerHoods\xe2\x80\x9d with more affordable housing, new types of manufacturing, better transportation, and a cleaner environment.advertisementThe Dutch MountainsThe Dutch MountainsThis design imagines a building\xc2\xa0as a collection of services\xe2\x80\x93providing light, heat, upgradable walls and floors, and even food and furniture\xe2\x80\x93 rather than an object that is finished when construction stops. Sensors collect data designed to make the offices,\xc2\xa0hotel rooms, restaurants, and other parts of the multi-purpose building more comfortable, easier to use, and healthier as time goes on. The building is also designed to use energy, water, and other resources in sustainable, closed-loop systems.Avalon VillageAvalon VillageWhen the city turned off the streetlights in her neighborhood in Highland Park, Michigan\xe2\x80\x93because it couldn\xe2\x80\x99t afford the electric bill\xe2\x80\x93Shamayim \xe2\x80\x9cMama Shu\xe2\x80\x9d Harris partnered with a nonprofit to install a solar-powered light. Then she continued to transform her struggling block, buying up vacant lots to create an ecovillage. One\xc2\xa0lot became a community park, an abandoned garage will become a cafe, and a home rebuilt with geothermal and solar power will become a place for local children to study. When it\xe2\x80\x99s complete, Avalon Village will also include a community grocery store, affordable housing, a center for female entrepreneurs, and an urban farm.The Storefront TheaterMatthew MazzottaIn tiny Lyons, Nebraska, population 851, most of the businesses on Main Street have closed. At one store, all that was left of the building was a freestanding wall in front. Artist\xc2\xa0Matthew Mazzotta helped create a new use for the space:\xc2\xa0using hydraulic pumps, the wall lowers down to become seating for a new community theater.advertisementYoshino Cedar House\nAirbnb and Go HasegawaLike other parts of rural Japan, the small town of Yoshino has struggled as younger generations move away to cities. Airbnb worked with the town\xe2\x80\x93which is a popular place for cherry-blossom viewing\xe2\x80\x93to build a beautiful new building from local materials that can double as a community center and a place to host visitors.\xc2\xa0It\xe2\x80\x99s designed to foster interaction between locals and tourists and keep local traditions alive.The UnderlineJames Corner Field OperationsUnder Miami\xe2\x80\x99s MetroRail, underused space is turning into a 10-mile long urban park filled with green space, art, and better paths to walk and bike between neighborhoods in the southern part of the city and downtown Miami. The path will also connect with the East Coast Greenway, a 2,900-mile long bike and pedestrian path that goes from Maine to Florida.Corridors of PowerCentre for Policy AlternativesThis exhibition in Sri Lanka used architectural drawings and models as a way to visualize how the country\xe2\x80\x99s constitution has evolved since the 1970s. Through 3D designs, it illustrates the power dynamics at work in the constitution\xc2\xa0and\xc2\xa0the document\xe2\x80\x99s flaws.\nadvertisementNew Songdo CityKohn Pedersen Fox AssociatesThis newly-built district in South Korea, near the capital of Seoul, was designed to be as sustainable as possible. A\xc2\xa0Central Park-like green space fills the middle of the area. Residents can walk, bike, and take public transit so easily that they shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t ever need to drive, but shared electric cars are available. The district is designed to use 40% less energy than a typical development. By 2020, 40% of water will be recycled. Waste travels through pneumatic pipes instead of on garbage trucks.Heidelberg VillageFrey ArchitektenPart of the world\xe2\x80\x99s largest \xe2\x80\x9cpassive house\xe2\x80\x9d development, this new complex in Heidelberg, Germany, is designed to be both sustainable and have a social impact. The apartments\xc2\xa0bring together people of all ages. For the elderly, it offers on-site health care and handicapped accessibility. For young families, there\xe2\x80\x99s on-site child care. Solar panels on the walls provide shade in the summer and renewable energy all year.South Side SoapboxMethod Products and Gotham GreensBuilt on a brownfield site on Chicago\xe2\x80\x99s South Side, this LEED-certified factory has the world\xe2\x80\x99s largest rooftop farm\xc2\xa0on the top. Inside, manufacturers such as Method\xe2\x80\x93known for its sustainably-designed soap\xe2\x80\x93make products using the building\xe2\x80\x99s renewable energy. Half of the power comes from on-site sources such as solar and wind turbines, and the other half comes from renewable energy credits.advertisementLinkNYCIntersectionMaking use of New York City\xe2\x80\x99s obsolete pay phone booths\xe2\x80\x93more than 7,500 phones in five boroughs\xe2\x80\x93LinkNYC will be the largest free public wi-fi network in the world. The kiosks, which began rolling out in January 2016, also provide device charging, phone calls, and tablets that can access city maps and services.El-Space: Creating Dynamic Places Under the ElevatedDesign Trust for Public SpaceIn New York City, hundreds of miles of elevated rail and subway lines, highways, and bridges have created underused, often unpleasant space underneath.\xc2\xa0In the El-Space project, the city\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Transportation and the nonprofit\xc2\xa0Design Trust for Public Space are exploring ways to\xc2\xa0add lighting and green space beneath the infrastructure, reconnecting neighborhoods.The Brooklyn Strand Action PlanWXY Architecture + Urban DesignThis community-driven vision looks at how downtown Brooklyn\xe2\x80\x93which is currently filled with outdated, mid-20th-century car infrastructure\xe2\x80\x93could be better connected, creating a strand of walkable, bikeable paths between the center of downtown and the waterfront and nearby neighborhoods. In total, more than 80 acres of publicly-owned space would\xc2\xa0shift from use mostly by cars to use by pedestrians and cyclists, helping support the growth of a new innovation district.advertisementadvertisementadvertisementAbout the authorAdele Peters is a staff writer at Fast Company who focuses on solutions to some of the world's largest problems, from climate change to homelessness. adding to a collection of more than 100 he has discovered\nPrevious\nNext\nThe Crafty Traveller: The roaming fee tricks that everyone STILL needs to knowThe Mail on Sunday's Crafty Traveller shares his holiday expertise\xc2\xa0Roaming charges for using a mobile phone in most of Europe are now outlawedBut that doesn't mean pitfalls don't exist, as Frank Mawer explains here\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0By Fred Mawer For The Mail On Sunday\nPublished: 17:01 EDT, 15 July 2017\n|\nUpdated: 17:01 EDT, 15 July 2017\ne-mail\n6 shares\n1 View\ncomments\nFor\xc2\xa0many holidaymakers heading abroad this summer, one irksome cost has disappeared.\xc2\xa0Roaming charges for using a mobile phone in most of Europe were outlawed last month under European Commission rules.The changes mean we now pay the same as we do in the UK to make calls, send texts and use data when we are in any of the 27 other European Union countries.\nAs of last month, we now pay the same as we do in the UK to make calls, send texts and use data when we are in any of the 27 other European Union countriesThe new \xe2\x80\x98roam like at home\xe2\x80\x99 rules also apply in European Economic Area countries \xe2\x80\x93 Iceland, Liechtenstein and Norway.This is great news, but be warned: there are potential pitfalls. For example, don\xe2\x80\x99t fall into the trap of thinking that roaming is now free wherever you are in Europe.Some operators have extended roaming at no extra cost beyond EU countries \xe2\x80\x93 for example, with Vodafone to the Channel Islands, Albania, Switzerland and Turkey. However, with EE, O2 and Three, you still have to pay high fees to roam in Turkey.\nRELATED ARTICLES\nPrevious 1 Next\nBob along to Bodrum: Tourists are shying away from Turkey -...\nLondon to France on a PRIVATE PLANE for \xc2\xa361? New Uber-like...\nShare this article\nShare\nOperators are also allowed to impose \xe2\x80\x98fair use\xe2\x80\x99 restrictions for data usage where domestic plans include unlimited data, and charge if you exceed their limits.But while some operators have decided to set such a limit \xe2\x80\x93 with Three for a contract customer it is 12GB a month \xe2\x80\x93 not all are following suit, so check with your provider.Beyond those European countries where roaming charges have been abolished, staying connected when travelling can still be very expensive.\nSome operators have extended roaming at no extra cost beyond EU countries \xe2\x80\x93 for example, with Vodafone to Turkey (pictured). With EE, O2 and Three, though, this is not the caseWith O2, for example, the standard rate for pay-monthly customers in popular holiday destinations such as Barbados, Thailand and the United Arab Emirates is \xc2\xa31.50 a minute to make a call, \xc2\xa31.25 a minute to receive a call, 40p to send a text and \xc2\xa36 to use 1MB of data (1MB is a tiny amount \xe2\x80\x93 downloading a song typically uses at least 3MB).Moreover, from next month roaming charges outside the EU will be subject to 20 per cent VAT, so unless operators absorb the tax rise, rates may shoot up.But there are ways to avoid, or at least minimise, roaming costs outside the EU\xe2\x80\xa6Use Three\xc2\xa0Its Feel At Home arrangement, which lets customers roam using their UK call, text and data allowances, covers a number of major long-haul holiday destinations. These include the United States, Australia, New Zealand, Hong Kong and Sri Lanka, and Brazil and Singapore have just been added to the list.Just bear in mind that in these countries you still have to pay extra for calls to local numbers made within the destination you\xe2\x80\x99re visiting \xe2\x80\x93 such as making a reservation with a New York restaurant while you are in the Big Apple.Sign up for an add-on roaming package with other operatorsIt is likely to work out far cheaper than roaming on their standard rates. For example, the O2 Travel add-on, which pay-monthly customers can use in dozens of countries outside its Europe Zone, gives unlimited data, 120 minutes for calls and 120 texts for \xc2\xa34.99 a day.Use free wi-fiI cannot think of a hotel or self-catering rental I\xe2\x80\x99ve stayed at abroad in the past year which hasn\xe2\x80\x99t offered some free internet access. And a growing number of cities are offering free wi-fi hotspots, such as New York (see link.nyc).Even in EU countries where data roaming now costs nothing extra, it\xe2\x80\x99s better to use wi-fi so that you don\xe2\x80\x99t eat up any data allowances.You can track down free-access hotspots around the world on a wi-fi app (wifimap.io), and Facebook has also just started rolling out a feature for locating free wi-fi.With free wi-fi, you can make voice or video calls with family and friends on internet-enabled services such as Skype, WhatsApp and Apple\xe2\x80\x99s FaceTime without costing a penny. They really are the best way to stay in touch during your travels.\nAdvertisement\nShare or comment on this article:\nThe Crafty Traveller's roaming fee tricks\ne-mail\n6\nshares\nMost watched News videos\nMerchants tie woman to pole and set her feet on fire for stealing\nMark Field ejected Greenpeace protester after grabbing her neck\nEamonn bursts into tears as he explains why Ruth is not on the show\nMan films strippers next door during noisy house party\n12-year-old boy savagely beaten by two older school students\nCute video shows boy running to kitchen when he hears candy jar open\nBar staff 'takes swipe' at man after he refused to pay \xc2\xa31 for water\nLA county deputies shoot dead unarmed father of three\nMan starts huge brawl with TSA agents at Phoenix airport\nProtestor filmed being grabbed by Tory MP gives first interview\nHunt hugs his wife after realising he is close to the Tory crown\nPlayful pup peaks past curtains for some piquant popcorn\nComments 1\nShare what you think\nNewest\nOldest\nBest rated\nWorst rated\nView all\nThe comments below have not been moderated.\nView all\nThe views expressed in the contents above are those of our users and do not necessarily reflect the views of MailOnline.\nWe are no longer accepting comments on this article.\nMore top stories\nBing\nSite\nWeb\nEnter search term:\nSearch\nAdvertisement\nLike\nDailyMail\nFollow\nDailyMail\nFollow\n@dailymail\nFollow\nDailyMail\nFollow\nMailOnline\nFollow\nDaily Mail\nTOP STORIES IN TRAVEL\n'If they could get away with cutting out the bit where they put the plane in the air, they would': Etiquette expert William Hanson flies RYANAIR from Nice to London - and isn't impressed\nTime to kill, money to burn! 245 days. licensingAccount and SupportHelp and FAQContact usSign in / Create an accountManage your accountFollow MIT Technology Review \xc2\xa92019 v.|ei\xcf\x80|Simon LandreinBusiness ImpactThe Startup Behind NYC\xe2\x80\x99s Plan to Replace Phone Booths with 7,500 Connected KiosksIntersection, which is funded by Alphabet, hopes they could someday guide autonomous vehicles, too.by Elizabeth WoykeJul 18, 2017If you live in a big city, you\xe2\x80\x99ve probably experienced the frustration of rushing to the subway only to realize\xe2\x80\x94eventually\xe2\x80\x94that it\xe2\x80\x99s delayed and you would have been better off walking or taking the bus. What if there were digital screens mounted on street corners that warned you the subway was running late and directed you to other forms of transportation? And what if those screens also notified you of community events, listed daily pollution levels, and solicited your opinion on local government initiatives?Such a scenario may soon be reality in London and New York. Both cities are replacing outdated phone booths with Wi-Fi kiosks that have embedded computing tablets, USB charging ports, keypads for making phone calls, and large screens that display relevant information to passersby. New York, which started installing its \xe2\x80\x9cLinkNYC\xe2\x80\x9d kiosks in 2016, currently has more than 900 activated across all five boroughs and plans to increase that number to 7,500. The U.K.\xc2\xa0just started erecting its \xe2\x80\x9cInLinkUK\xe2\x80\x9d kiosks in London and\xc2\xa0intends to deploy up to 1,000 across the country.Today, people use the Links primarily to charge their smartphones, take advantage of the fast Wi-Fi, make Internet (VoIP) calls, and search for information about the weather and local restaurants. All these services are free to use, in part because the 10-foot-tall kiosks display ads that generate funds the cities share with the companies that designed and run the technology. These companies, which include Qualcomm and the telecom giant BT, pay for the Links\xe2\x80\x99 installation and maintenance costs. They have estimated that the city of New York will earn more than half a billion dollars in revenue over 12 years from the LinkNYC partnership.A LinkNYC Wi-Fi kiosk on the street. Intersection runs more than 900 of these across New York City.Link is poised to be far more than an advertising and Wi-Fi network, however. Intersection, the company that manages the Link projects in London and New York, is considering upgrading them to support everything from augmented reality to autonomous vehicles. \xe2\x80\x9cPhase One was about making sure we\xe2\x80\x99re offering robust services to people,\xe2\x80\x9d says Intersection\xe2\x80\x99s chief innovation officer, Colin O\xe2\x80\x99Donnell. \xe2\x80\x9cNow we\xe2\x80\x99re figuring out how we can leverage all the different data sets we have access to and make [this technology] as dynamic and responsive as it can be.\xe2\x80\x9dIntersection\xe2\x80\x99s ambitions bear attention because it is one of the few private firms that large cities have partnered with on high-profile public-information projects\xe2\x80\x94and its digital technology is likely to spread to other major U.S. cities, such as Chicago, San Francisco, and Seattle, where it holds multiyear municipal and transit advertising contracts. (That\xe2\x80\x99s true despite public concern last year that some people were using the LinkNYC kiosks to watch inappropriate videos and blast music. Intersection says it disabled the Internet browser on the kiosks\xe2\x80\x99 tablets in September 2016 and has received very few complaints since.)Sign up for The Download \xe2\x80\x94 your daily dose of what's up in emerging technologyAlso stay updated on MIT Technology Review initiatives and events?YesNoIntersection\xe2\x80\x99s vision for the future may also suggest ways that Google parent Alphabet hopes to shape cities through its \xe2\x80\x9curban innovation\xe2\x80\x9d subsidiary, Sidewalk Labs. Sidewalk Labs is an investor in Intersection, its CEO is the chairman of Intersection\xe2\x80\x99s board of directors, and the companies share the same Manhattan office. O\xe2\x80\x99Donnell declined to comment on his company\xe2\x80\x99s association with Alphabet beyond saying that he collaborates frequently with Sidewalk Labs on smart-city ideas, with Intersection tackling the more immediate work and Sidewalk Labs focusing on projects that are five or more years out. But it\xe2\x80\x99s easy to see how the companies could sync up on future initiatives.Since Intersection\xe2\x80\x99s LinkNYC and InLinkUK contracts both run for at least 10 years, O\xe2\x80\x99Donnell has been brainstorming new features that would make the kiosks more useful. For example, the Links could be outfitted with environmental sensors. Intersection worked with Argonne National Laboratory to develop sensors that detect about 30 different pollutants and could negotiate with its city partners to add them to the kiosks.Intersection also manages 185 information kiosks inside the New York City subway.Each Link also has two built-in cameras, which face in opposite directions, potentially yielding views up and down the street. Right now, these cameras are only used to monitor for vandalism and damage, but if the city granted permission, Intersection could use them to capture a nearly 360\xc2\xb0 view of each Link\xe2\x80\x99s surroundings. (Intersection says it does not store video for longer than seven days, unless the footage is necessary to investigate an incident. The company also says it does not use facial recognition technology or track people\xe2\x80\x99s movement through the city.) Eventually, information from Intersection\xe2\x80\x99s future sensors could be combined to create real-time data maps that might be useful for emerging technologies such as self-driving cars.Joseph Chow, an assistant professor of civil and urban engineering at New York University, likes the idea of Intersection using its kiosks as city sensors. He thinks future Links could help facilitate a Department of Transportation project that is researching ways to use roadside infrastructure to communicate information about accidents to cars and other vehicles. \xe2\x80\x9cThese technologies provide the architecture that smart cities need to operate,\xe2\x80\x9d says Chow. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you use them to collect information about how people are traveling and to detect disruptions, you can react to situations faster and make better decisions.\xe2\x80\x9dNext, Intersection is looking to deploy its digital screens in airports, apartment buildings, and office complexes. O\xe2\x80\x99Donnell says the company has spent \xe2\x80\x9ctens of thousands of hours\xe2\x80\x9d in airports studying ways that connected displays could guide people from arrival through the security process and to their gates. Intersection has also worked with real estate developers, including New York\xe2\x80\x93based Related Companies, to streamline the way people enter and navigate buildings, move through security, and learn about tenant news and events. Its ultimate goal, says O\xe2\x80\x99Donnell, is to build a \xe2\x80\x9cdynamic digital infrastructure across the entire city experience.\xe2\x80\x9dShareLinkTaggedSmart CitiesAuthorElizabeth 2019\nJun\n23\nEvents\nBuena Onda: Music from South America\n12:00 AM\nSingles Social & Dance\n12:00 AM\nmore\nadd\nFacebookTwitteremail\nFacebookTwitteremail\nLinkNYC kiosks showcase southeast Queens artists\nPhoto by Naeisha Rose\nLinkNYC kiosks will feature work from local artists throughout the Jamaica area.\n[email\xc2\xa0protected]\n/\nMonday, October 30, 2017\n/\n12:00 AM\nBy Naeisha Rose\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s been two years since the launch of LinkNYC citywide and the free Wi-Fi connection service has truly been utilized by businesses in Jamaica, and now by local artists.\nGreg Mays, the founder\nof A Better Jamaica \xe2\x80\x94 a non-profit community service arts organization \xe2\x80\x94 is curating artwork by southeast Queens and New York City artists on the LinkNYC kiosks, which have been slowly replacing the 7,500 pay phones across the five boroughs with public Wi-Fi charging stations.\nIndividuals can make phone calls on any of the 1,000 kiosks, which have tablets to access city services, maps and directions, according to the organization.\nBusinesses on Jamaica Avenue from Sutphin Boulevard to 168th Street have embraced the kiosks to by advertising on them.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have had fans of our salon send us photos of our salon being promoted on the LinkNYC screens. It\xe2\x80\x99s so fun to see them engage with our brand!\xe2\x80\x9d said Maria Delgado of Yvelisse Salon.\nThe kiosks started to include monthlong art exhibits by local artists Oct. 14, Mays said.\nHe was inspired to feature artwork by area artists in public spaces after seeing the same mural work by the Jamaica Center Parsons/Archer station for years and he wanted to do something fresh.\nAt first he reached out to the Metropolitan Transit Authority to feature artwork in the light boxes within the station that had old podiatrist ads, but Jamaica Center for Arts and Learning, a different art organization in the area had artwork put up in the station.\nAfter a year of conceiving this project, Mays got in touch with Melva Miller, the deputy borough president, who put him in touch with LinkNYC.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to displace what JCAL was doing,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mays, \xe2\x80\x9cso I reached out to the LinkNYC people.\xe2\x80\x9d\nThe first artist to have his artwork displayed on the kiosks is Emmett Wigglesworth, 83.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI was excited when I heard they were going to feature artists on the kiosks,\xe2\x80\x9d Wigglesworth said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve been an artist all my life and I enjoy doing it.\xe2\x80\x9d\nWigglesworth became a professional artist in 1957 after finishing his service with the Marine Corps during the Korean War and has lived in the Jamaica area since.\nHis artwork falls in the fauvism style, which emphasizes strong color over realistic representation of people or objects. Some of Wigglesworth art on the kiosks features people playing jazz music on saxophones. Southeast Queens use to be home to many jazz musicians like John Coltrane, who lived in St. Albans.\n\xe2\x80\x9cAll the news about southeast Queens is about the foreclosures going on, but he knew it\xe2\x80\x99s much more than that,\xe2\x80\x9d Mays said.\nThere are 10 pieces of Wigglesworth art featured on 18 kiosks on Jamaica Avenue from Sutphin Boulevard to 168th Street, which will be there until the end of October.\nReach reporter Naeisha Rose by e-mail at nrose@cnglocal.com or by phone at (718) 260\xe2\x80\x934573.\nTopics:\nart\nGreg Mays\nShare this story\nFacebookTwitteremail\nRelated Stories\nArtisanal craft program coming to St. Albans\nFilm program teaches black history through art\nPopular Stories\nFlushing man wins $5,000,000 on \'Set for Life\' scratch-off ticket\nThief drugged man\'s drink and stole his valuables while he slept in Queens home: cops\nLong Island City strip mall to get BJ\xe2\x80\x99s and Burlington Coat Factory\nAbout Schneps Communications, 2018\nMasthead\nPrivacy Policy\nTerms of Service\nQUEENS COURIER\nRIDGEWOOD TIMES\nBORO MAGAZINE\nLIC MAGAZINE\nSend Invite\n\xc3\x97\nSubject: Subject line is fixed\nAn invitation to join the QNS community.\n(optional) Customize the text of the\ninvitation.\nThe message will also contain a custom footer containing links to accept\nthe invitation or opt out of further email invitations from this site.\nYou have been invited by Queens Courier Staff to join the QNS community.\nVisit Queens Courier Staff\'s profile at qns.com/members/admin/.\n\xc3\x97\nCreate an Account\nForgot Password\nor\nLog in with\nCreate New Event\n\xc3\x97\nx\nUpload\nImproper image submitted. Sites\nWeb Adv.\nSections\nPrime Times\nHome & Garden\nBanking & Finance\nHealth & Fitness\nSchool Spotlight\nCelebration\nFall Guide\nAnniversary\nSpring Guide\nDigital Edition\nSouth Edition\nSpecial Sections\nPage One\nSports\nHome\nEditions\nQueenswide\nLinkNYC kiosks a boon to Queens biz\nJamaica retailers use Wi-Fi hotspot advertising space to self-promote\nStoryComments (1)\nPrint\nCreate a hardcopy of this page\nFont Size:\nDefault font size\nLarger font size\nPrevious\nNext\nPHOTO BY ANTHONY MEDINA\nLinkNYC kiosks a boon to Queens biz 1\nA LinkNYC kiosk located at 148th Street and Jamaica Avenue in front of the J City supermarket and steps away from the Cici Beauty Salon and Barber Shop.\nPosted: Thursday, November 9, 2017 10:30 am\nLinkNYC kiosks a boon to Queens biz\nby Anthony Medina, Chronicle Contributor\nQueens Chronicle\n|\n1\xc2\xa0comment\nLinkNYC has placed 1,399 of its Wi-Fi kiosks across New York City almost two years after its launch. The stations were placed around the city near transit stops and businesses, replacing old telephone booths.\nBusiness owners with kiosks in front of their stores in Jamaica have been using the advertising capabilities of LinkNYC to boost customer traffic and profits since their release.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are excited to work with the Jamaica BID and local small businesses to give them the opportunity to advertise on Links,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ruth Fasoldt, the community affairs manager for LinkNYC. \xe2\x80\x9cLocal ads run on two 55-inch digital displays on the Link closest to each business. Over 15 businesses along Jamaica Ave have participated thus far and we have gotten great feedback.\xe2\x80\x9d\nLinkNYC Wi-Fi can bring free services like phone calls and wireless web access to the city because of its paid advertising program. Its latest efforts citywide allow for business owners to advertise on booths closer to their area.\nValerie Stevens, the director of business services at the Jamaica Center Business Improvement District, says she\xe2\x80\x99s seen an increase in walk-ins at individually owned businesses and a change in aesthetics on Jamaica Avenue.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s great to have it here,\xe2\x80\x9d said Stevens. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a great marketing tool for the businesses on Jamaica Avenue. It promotes the avenue in a way that says this is marketable, there is revenue and businesses here.\xe2\x80\x9d\nStevens helped multiple stores advertise on the kiosks and gain the attention of larger audiences. In a back-to-school fashion show event hosted by the Jamaica Bid in August, Stevens said, she received a much larger crowd than expected thanks to the advertisements.\nMaria Delgado from Yvelisse Salon talked to LinkNYC about how her profits have increased since the placement of the kiosks.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have recently had an ad (thanks to LinkNYC and JBID for sponsoring us) entered onto the LinkNYC screens,\xe2\x80\x9d said Delgado said in an email to the Chronicle. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have had fans of our salon send us photos of our salon being promoted on the LinkNYC screens. It\xe2\x80\x99s so fun to see them engage with our brand!\xe2\x80\x9d\nStevens\xe2\x80\x99 talks with LinkNYC helped generate two months advertising on kiosks across the Jamaica strip for some businesses. Stevens planned to hold another meeting with LinkNYC to expand advertising to other boroughs and create a better package for Jamaica businesses.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think our businesses should be offered a reasonable fee to promote,\xe2\x80\x9d said Stevens. \xe2\x80\x9cThe businesses really liked seeing their brand on the machines. Our businesses should be given first choice to promote because they will be making money within the district.\xe2\x80\x9d\nMayor de Blasio\xe2\x80\x99s office announced the choice of CityBridge as the 12-year franchise agreement winner to orchestrate the LinkNYC program on Nov. 17, 2014. The project was set to replace public pay-phone booths with the latest technology.\nTechnological companies CityBridge, Intersection, Qualcomm and CIVIQ Smartscapes coordinated to make the kiosk stations user-friendly with a touch screen pad and slim design.\nAntenna Design, the tech company responsible for the kiosks\xe2\x80\x99 structure, made them to withstand the extreme weather conditions of New York like floods and snowstorms, and even earthquakes, according to LinkNYC.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere are more than 1,100 active Links in all five boroughs and thousands more are coming over the next few years,\xe2\x80\x9d said Fasoldt. \xe2\x80\x9cEach Link offers superfast Wi-Fi, phone calls, a 911 button and other services completely for free. Working with neighborhood businesses is a key part of our mission to make Link an integral part of the communities we deploy.\xe2\x80\x9d\nNearly 163 Links are placed around Queens on bus, train and traffic routes. That means almost 12 percent of kiosks in the city are in Queens.\nAlong Jamaica Avenue between 76th and 168th streets, there are 51 kiosks, according to the LinkNYC website map.\nQueens Boulevard holds the most in the borough between 78th Avenue and Van Dam Street with 54. Roosevelt Avenue falls in second with 35 booths between 72nd and Warren streets. Broadway between Corona Avenue and 75th Street holds 31 kiosks with other areas in the single digits.\nA representative from Make Me Over Beauty Bar on Jamaica Avenue and Merrick Boulevard talked to LinkNYC about how they encourage customers to use the Links.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe recommend LinkNYC to our customers daily when they ask for free Wi-Fi service,\xe2\x80\x9d the company said, in an email sent to the Chronicle. \xe2\x80\x9cThe comfort of the nearby kiosk provides free Wi-Fi to our customers sitting in the waiting area.\xe2\x80\x9d\nMore about Economy\nARTICLE: Hotels for sale spark shelter concerns\n$92.8 billion budget approved for city 1\nARTICLE: $92.8 billion budget approved for city\nCrossing all the Ts for Bartlett Dairy 1\nARTICLE: Crossing all the Ts for Bartlett Dairy\nDiscuss\nPrint\nPosted in\nQueenswide,\nSouth Queens News,\nEastern/Southeast Queens News,\nCentral/Mid Queens News,\nNorth/Northeast Queens News,\nWestern Queens News\non\nThursday, November 9, 2017 10:30 am.\n| Tags:\nEconomy\nWelcome to the discussion.\nLog In\nSign Up\n1 comment:\nVBarbour\nposted at 2:11 pm on Fri, Nov 10, 2017.\nPosts: 50\nFour years ago at a Participatory Budgeting (PB) session being held in NYC Council District 32 sponsored by the WRBA residents attending the event suggested that NYC provide WiFi for the businesses along the Jamaica Avenue in Woodhaven.\nWhen the suggestion was reviewed by City agencies we were told that the infrastructure would be too expensive and that the service could not be provided under PB rules.\nWe suggested it would still be a good idea.Now we find that 12 LinkNYC kiosks have been erected on Jamaica Avenue and that the public-private partnership between NYC and Alphabet (Google's parent) is generating $500 million in advertising revenue.\nSo what couldn't be done before can now magically be done when it generates revenue for The City.\nWhat I was expecting this article to address was that local business cannot afford the $5K it costs to advertise for 4 weeks on the LinkNYC kiosk and that local businesses still do not have free or low cost internet access to help generate business, create jobs and add tax revenue to NYC coffers.Maybe a follow-up story is in order?\nLink\nPrint comments\nSubmit your news!\nSubmit your news! Create one now.", b"What are those tall kiosks that have replaced pay phones in New York? - The New York Times\nSectionsSEARCHSkip to contentSkip to site indexNew YorkSubscribeLog InLog InToday\xe2\x80\x99s PaperNew York|What are those tall kiosks that have replaced pay phones in New York?AdvertisementSupported byF.Y.I.What are those tall kiosks that have replaced pay phones in New York?ImageSince the system launched in early 2016, around 1,250 Links have been erected throughout all five boroughs. The company is aiming for a total of 7,500 Links by 2026.CreditCreditCole Wilson for The New York TimesBy Keith WilliamsJan. 11, 2018Q. Tall kiosks labeled \xe2\x80\x9cLinkNYC\xe2\x80\x9d are replacing phone booths, offering free Wi-Fi and nationwide phone calls. The thing is, I have never seen anybody using one. What gives?A. Compared with the pay phones they often replace, LinkNYC kiosks, known as Links, get plenty of use, even if no one is standing next to them.According to CityBridge, the consortium that operates LinkNYC, over 3.2 million people have registered for the system\xe2\x80\x99s Wi-Fi service, with 600,000 users each week. The Wi-Fi operates at gigabit speed, meaning it can be up to 100 times faster than cellular LTE networks. The range of a Link is about 150 feet in any direction.Links are a critical piece in the city\xe2\x80\x99s goal to bring broadband internet access to all New Yorkers, but the system\xe2\x80\x99s community-first approach provides other social benefits, as well.Each Link has an interactive screen, which offers everyday information you might expect, like weather, local maps, and transit updates, as well as a connection to the city\xe2\x80\x99s 311 service. Through a partnership with the software program Aunt Bertha, however, users can anonymously search for nonprofit and social services.Links also offer free phone calls anywhere in the country; the system registers around 200,000 calls each month. The number dialed most frequently? The state\xe2\x80\x99s hotline for its Electronic Benefits Transfer program, commonly known as food stamps.Since the system launched in early 2016, around 1,250 Links have been erected throughout all five boroughs. The company is aiming for a total of 7,500 Links by 2026, when its contract with the city is scheduled to expire.As the first system of its kind, LinkNYC has faced unforeseen difficulties. When the system was introduced, each Link offered an internet browser. But a slew of complaints of users camping out in front of the units and, in some cases, viewing inappropriate content, caused the system to remove that functionality.The system\xe2\x80\x99s biggest challenge is finding new locations, said Jen Hensley, the general manager of LinkNYC. The system is building a new fiber-optic network, but not every pay phone site is close enough to a manhole to connect to it.Links generate revenue through advertisements, which appear on the 55-inch screens on the sides of each kiosk. These ads are interspersed with in-house content like \xe2\x80\x9cNYC Fun Facts\xe2\x80\x9d and historical photos of nearby locations. LinkNYC and the city split the ad revenue equally, subject to an annual minimum.The idea is expanding to other cities: Links have begun appearing in the United Kingdom, and are set to arrive in Philadelphia this summer.The system is in a constant state of refinement, with temporary options ranging from time-sensitive to whimsical. Through Jan. 31, for example, users can browse and enroll in health care plans; in December, each Link offered a direct line to Santa\xe2\x80\x99s voice mail.EMAIL fyi@nytimes.com A version of this article appears in print on , on Page MB3 of the New York edition. Archpaper.com\nLinkNYC kiosks will display iconic film director\xe2\x80\x99s photos of old New York\nMenu\nAwards\nAdvertise\nSubscribe\nContact\nAbout\nPrivacy Policy\nMap\nEvents\nCompetitions\nProducts\nJobs\nTopics\nRegions\nInternational\nEast\nSoutheast\nMidwest\nWest\nSouthwest\nTopics\nAN Interior\nArchitecture\nArt\nDesign\nDevelopment\nPreservation\nTransportation\nUrbanism\nNewsletters\nFacades+\nSpec Sheet\nCity Terrain\nLate Edition: East\nLate Edition: West\nLate Edition: Midwest\nLate Edition: Southwest\nConferences\nFacades+ Conference\nFacades+ AM\nTech+\nEvents\nCompetitions\nProducts\nJobs\nConferences\nConferences\nFacades+ Conferences\nTech+ Expo\nAwards\nSubscribe\nKubrick Takeover\nLinkNYC kiosks will display iconic film director\xe2\x80\x99s photos of old New York\nBy\nSelina Cheah\n\xe2\x80\xa2\nJune 19, 2018\nShare:\nBeginning this Thursday, LinkNYC kiosks around the city will feature images from the Museum of the City of New York\xe2\x80\x99s (MCNY) extensive photography archive.\nThe aptly named campaign, Summer in the City, is a partnership between the Department of Information Technology & Telecommunications (DoITT), LinkNYC, the city\xe2\x80\x99s free Wi-Fi kiosk system, and MCNY. Images will be displayed from the Museum\xe2\x80\x99s current exhibition, Through a Different Lens: Stanley Kubrick Photographs.\nPasserby on the street will be able to catch a glimpse of the old New York through the lens of the iconic film director. Kubrick\xe2\x80\x99s photographs highlight his formative years as a photographer (before he became a film director) for Look magazine in New York City between 1945-1950. The photographs focus on and capture the pathos of everyday life of the city, from street scenes to sporting events.\nThe LinkNYC kiosks can be found dotted all over the city. Since Mayor Bill de Blasio launched the program in 2016, more than 1,650 Links are active across all five boroughs and have replaced the old pay phones with sleek kiosks that feature free Wi-Fi, phone chargers, and digital displays for advertisements and in this case, art.\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not the first time that LinkNYC has featured art on its kiosks from MCNY. Previous \xe2\x80\x9cexhibitions\xe2\x80\x9d on the kiosks include historic photos of women who influenced New York\xe2\x80\x99s political history for Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month and \xe2\x80\x9cOn This Day in NYC History\xe2\x80\x9d information. The MCNY and LinkNYC partnership is one of many programs that disseminate New York City\xe2\x80\x99s history; others include the NYC Space/Time Directory from the New York Public Library, an app from Urban Archive that made more than 2,500 images of old New York available on-the-go, and a Civil Rights & Social Justice Map from the Greenwich Village Society.\nLinkNYC\nMCNY\nPublic Art\nRelated 21 Murray Street, 5th Floor | New York, NY 10007 | tel. 212.966.0630\nCopyright 2019, All rights reserved.", b"LinkNYC kiosks showcase work by locals during National Poetry Month | am New York\nMenu\nLATEST PAPER\nSEARCH\nNews\nPolitics\nThings To Do\nEAT & DRINK\nEntertainment\nReal Estate\nTransit\nOpinion\nLATEST PAPER\n79\xc2\xb0\n6/23/2019\nGood Afternoon\nSEARCH\nHome\nNews\nPolitics\nElections\nThings To Do\nEat & Drink\nEntertainment\nCelebrities\nPets\nSecrets of NY\nReal Estate\nCity Living\nBrooklyn\nManhattan\nQueens\nStaten Island\nTransit\nSports\nOpinion\nJim Marguiles\nCartoon roundup\nWeather\n79\xc2\xb0\n6/23/2019\nGood Afternoon\nNews\nLinkNYC kiosks showcase work by locals during National Poetry Month\nPoems were composed by those with HIV/AIDS and other conditions.\nLinkNYC kiosks are displaying work by Alliance for Positive Change's clients for\nNational Poetry Month.\nPhoto Credit: Alliance for Positive Change\nBy Lisa L. Colangelo lisa.colangelo@amny.com\n@lisalcolangelo\nUpdated April 15, 2018 4:59 PM\nPrint\nShare\nfbShare\nTweet\nEmail\nWhile you are charging your phone at a LinkNYC kiosk this month, take a minute and soak in some poetry.\nThe electronic information boards will feature poems by clients of the Alliance for Positive Change, a nonprofit that helps people living with HIV/AIDS and other chronic illnesses.\nFor more than 15 years, the organization has offered creative writing classes that provide a safe and powerful outlet for people to express their life experiences.\nSome of the work has been featured in Situations, an annual literary journal and shared through live readings.\nBut this is the first time the work is being highlighted using 1,500 LinkNYC kiosks around the five boroughs through a partnership with the city\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Information Technology and Telecommunications in honor of National Poetry Month.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe wanted to provide an opportunity other than support groups, something that provided intellectual stimulation,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sharen Duke, executive director and CEO of the alliance. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you could utilize writing to express your fears, your trauma, your hopes, it can build self-esteem, recovery and healing.\xe2\x80\x9d\nRosa Velez, a former client, now helps facilitate the classes. Writing helped Velez deal with her deep depression and grief after her partner passed away while waiting for a liver transplant.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI wanted a place where I could express what I was feeling but I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t really sure what I was feeling,\xe2\x80\x9d Velez said. \xe2\x80\x9cI was hurt and angry.\xe2\x80\x9d\nGet Breaking News emails\nThe latest about your city, as it happens.\nSign up\nBy clicking Sign up, you agree to our privacy policy.\nHer writing group turned into a second family. And she now strives to share that support with other clients who might be intimidated by the idea of writing poetry.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe tell them to write from the heart,\xe2\x80\x9d Velez said, adding that she leaves each session with a feeling of hope.\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt inspires me to come back and teach the class,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\nDuke said the writing groups, which meet weekly, have been held more than 800 times since starting in 2000 and have collectively created thousands of poems.\nShe reached out to her friend, Gerry Gomez Pearlberg, a writer and poet, to help design the class. Pearlberg trained students, such as Velez, to be leaders and carry the program forward.\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe respected the way we were feeling and always made us feel comfortable,\xe2\x80\x9d Velez said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe told us to write whatever we were feeling that day and it was OK.\xe2\x80\x9d\nSince some of the sensitive subject matter that comes up in discussions and in writing includes violence, abuse, rape and substance abuse, confidentiality is key, Velez said.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhatever you say in the class stays in the class,\xe2\x80\x9d Velez said.\nExplaining the program to funders has sometimes been a challenge because they question how it can help with HIV prevention and other health issues, Duke said. But she is able to share examples of the program\xe2\x80\x99s positive impacts, for instance, one client proudly told Duke he spent his last dollar laminating his poem rather than purchasing a beer.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhen a person feels respected, feels heard, feels good about themselves, they will be in a better place to take care of themselves,\xe2\x80\x9d Duke said.\nBy Lisa L. Colangelo lisa.colangelo@amny.com\n@lisalcolangelo\nLisa joined amNewYork as a staff writer in 2017. All rights reserved.", b"The Facts Behind the New York City Facts \xe2\x80\x93 Next City\nInspiring Better Cities\nMenu\nSign Up\nTwitter\nFacebook\nLinkedIn\nRSS\nsearch\nLatest News\nBecome a Member\nLogin\nFAQ\nFeatures\nLatest Feature\nEbooks\nTopics\nTechCultureEconomicsHousingTransportation & InfrastructureEnergy & Environment\nVanguard\nHost Vanguard\nSponsor Vanguard\nApply for Vanguard\nVanguards\nEvents\nJobs\nPost a Job Listing\nFind a Job\nTwitter\nFacebook\nLinkedIn\nRSS\nAbout Next City\nContact\nAdvertise\nPitch a Story\nNewsletter\nPress Room\nMeet the Experts\n\xc3\x97\nFacebook\nTwitter\nEmail\nThe Facts Behind the New York City Facts\nSamantha Maldonado \xc2\xa0 \xc2\xa0 March 19, 2018\nFacebook\nTwitter\nEmail\nA LinkNYC Kiosk on the street in Queens (Credit:\xc2\xa0DanTD)\nBerry Villegas walks his dog at least twice a day, once in the morning and once at night. Along the way, Villegas scopes out the silver LinkNYC kiosks. These 10-foot-tall, silver monoliths have replaced sidewalk payphones in more than 1,300 locations throughout the five boroughs. The kiosks provide free WiFi and calling functions and allow users to charge their phones.\nRelated Stories\nBridging Detroit\xe2\x80\x99s Digital Divide Has Community MeaningPublic Service Design Brings Fresh Eyes to Old ProblemsNew York City to Subsidize MetroCards for Low-Income ResidentsNew York Lawmakers Making More Moves Against Tenant Harassment\nVillegas looks to the gleaming, 55-inch screens on either side of the kiosks, seeking new additions to a series of numbered New York City facts, rotating among the paid advertisements, event listings, weather updates and transit alerts. If Villegas, 44, comes across a fact that strikes his fancy, he posts a picture of it on Instagram.\nHis family and friends back in Florida, where he lived before moving to the city in June, now know that there is a superhero supply store in Brooklyn (fact number 139), that New York City gets 15 times more snow than the South Pole each year (fact number 206) and that Martin Hildebrandt opened the United States\xe2\x80\x99 first tattoo business in New York City in 1870 (fact number 304).\n\xe2\x80\x9cThose are just things that stop you in your tracks and you go, huh, I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know that,\xe2\x80\x9d Villegas says. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s nice to not just see someone selling me a phone plan or a movie trailer. It\xe2\x80\x99s nice to see just facts.\xe2\x80\x9d\nThat\xe2\x80\x99s the intention of Amanda Giddon, the woman behind the facts. Giddon works at Intersection, the company that manages the LinkNYC kiosks (soon to expand the network to Philadelphia). In addition to their primary functions, the kiosks host advertising and more than 50 other content campaigns, such as news headlines, information on how to sign up for health insurance, a series of comics, and the facts. The ads are on track to generate half a billion dollars in revenue over the next 12 years \xe2\x80\x94 enough to cover the cost of the LinkNYC kiosk services.\nGiddon, 24, grew up in the New York suburbs, and still remembers the sense of awe she felt every time she rode the train thirty minutes into the city \xe2\x80\x94 a feeling she still experiences.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThrough this work, I\xe2\x80\x99ve definitely re-connected with the city in a new way,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. Her interest in historical New York led her to recently pick up Jennifer Egan\xe2\x80\x99s novel \xe2\x80\x9cManhattan Beach.\xe2\x80\x9d She is eager to try Enoteca Maria, an Italian restaurant in Staten Island that features the cooking of a different grandmother each night. She heard about the restaurant during her fact research.\nGiddon kicked off the NYC Facts campaign in early 2017, right when she started at Intersection. Before then, she\xe2\x80\x99d been working in digital media for almost two years, after graduating from Duke University in 2015.\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy goal with this campaign is to really make New Yorkers feel like tourists and tourists like New Yorkers,\xe2\x80\x9d Giddon says. \xe2\x80\x9cThe strategy is making [LinkNYC kiosks] a beloved member of the community and making life more enjoyable as people navigate the city.\xe2\x80\x9d\nAs of this writing, Giddon has curated 349 facts and rolls out new ones on a weekly basis. The Intersection communications team gives the facts a quick review before the they go live. What makes a good fact? \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s something that can surprise and delight even the most seasoned New Yorker who\xe2\x80\x99s lived decades in the city,\xe2\x80\x9d says Giddon, \xe2\x80\x9cAnd also can arm consumers with things they want to share with their friends.\xe2\x80\x9d\nIt can be a challenge, especially if you\xe2\x80\x99re trying to surprise long-time New Yorkers. Giddon spends a few hours a week fact-hunting, which gives her an opportunity to follow her curiosity. From perusing Broadway.org, she learned that only five of the 40 Broadway theaters are actually on Broadway. According to data from Grow NYC, Greenmarket farmers travel an average of 90 miles between their farm and the city. She found that New Yorkers bite 10 times more people than sharks do worldwide while reading a Time magazine article. When FiveThirtyEight published a report on elevators in New York, the fact that 18 percent of the city\xe2\x80\x99s adult population could be riding in elevators at a time caught Giddon\xe2\x80\x99s eye.\nA partnership with the National History Museum\xe2\x80\x99s StarTalk Radio resulted in a series of celestial-themed facts. Giddon also worked with the Department of Records to create a series of historical photos displayed on kiosks in the neighborhoods where the photos were originally taken. Her plan to attend the Women\xe2\x80\x99s March inspired a group of facts about women\xe2\x80\x99s history and the suffrage movement in New York, all on display during the event.\nGiddon keeps track of her facts on a spreadsheet and estimates that about two-thirds of the facts in her collection haven\xe2\x80\x99t been published. Sometimes coworkers and friends will suggest facts to include, but Giddon must verify the facts before publishing them. Giddon finds the facts about firsts, such as the origins of the first cappuccino or Manhattan cocktail, to be the most difficult to pin down.\n\xe2\x80\x9cPeople feel so strongly about New York culture and history that I make it my duty to make sure we\xe2\x80\x99re putting the right stuff out there,\xe2\x80\x9d Giddon says with a laugh, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cIf something is wrong, we totally will get called out on it.\xe2\x80\x9d\nBecome A Next City Member Today\nSign-up for our newsletters\nSign Up\nSamantha Maldonado is\xc2\xa0a multimedia journalist based in New York City. She's\xc2\xa0interested in stories about cities, health, and culture. Mascali\nPublished : March 08, 2018\nFacebook\nTwitter\nLinkedIn\nReddit\nWhatsapp\nEmail\nMore\nShare this article\nFacebook\nTwitter\nMail\nWhatsapp\nReddit\nLinkedIn\n1/3\nStarting on International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day and running throughout the rest of Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month, LinkNYC will honor city\xe2\x80\x99s trailblazing women political activists. (MCNY)\n1/3\nStarting on International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day and running throughout the rest of Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month, LinkNYC will honor city\xe2\x80\x99s trailblazing women political activists. (MCNY)\n1/3\nStarting on International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day and running throughout the rest of Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month, LinkNYC will honor city\xe2\x80\x99s trailblazing women political activists. (MCNY)\n2/3\nStarting on International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day and running throughout the rest of Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month, LinkNYC will honor city\xe2\x80\x99s trailblazing women political activists. (MCNY)\n2/3\nStarting on International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day and running throughout the rest of Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month, LinkNYC will honor city\xe2\x80\x99s trailblazing women political activists. (MCNY)\n3/3\nThe initiative is in conjunction with the Museum of the City of New York\xe2\x80\x99s current exhibit, \xe2\x80\x98Beyond Suffrage: A Century of New York Women in Politics.\xe2\x80\x99 (MCNY)\n3/3\nThe initiative is in conjunction with the Museum of the City of New York\xe2\x80\x99s current exhibit, \xe2\x80\x98Beyond Suffrage: A Century of New York Women in Politics.\xe2\x80\x99 (MCNY)\nBack to top\nFacebook\nTwitter\nLinkedIn\nReddit\nWhatsapp\nEmail\nFor more than a century, International Women\xe2\x80\x99s Day has celebrated the social, economic, cultural and political achievements of women across the globe. And starting today through the rest of the month, some of New York City\xe2\x80\x99s most trailblazing female political activists will be honored at LinkNYC kiosks across the city.\nThe initiative is a collaboration between LinkNYC, the city\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Information Technology and Telecommunications (DoITT) and the Museum of the City of New York and not only commemorates this year\'s IWD, but also March being Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month.\nThe women featured on the LinkNYC kiosks are included in the museum\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cBeyond Suffrage: A Century of New York Women in Politics\xe2\x80\x9d exhibit, which runs through Aug. 5.\nRecommended Slideshows\n40 PicturesPHOTOS: Blues dump Bruins to win Stanley Cup after agonizing 52-year wait40 Pictures\n8 PicturesPHOTOS: This Pakistani waiter looks just like Peter Dinklage8 Pictures\n36 PicturesAll of these celebrities have had their nudes leaked36 PicturesMore picture galleries\n16 PicturesThese photos of Trump and Ivanka will make you deeply uncomfortable\n16 Pictures\n4 PicturesCuba Gooding Jr. charged in Manhattan groping incident, police say4 Pictures\n2 Pictures4 fun things to do in the Lehigh Valley2 Pictures\n\xe2\x80\x9cDuring Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month, we are proud to shine a light on prominent women who have positively impacted New York City and the entire nation,\xe2\x80\x9d said Jen Hensley, president of LinkNYC. \xe2\x80\x9cUsing Link\xe2\x80\x99s platform of digital displays throughout the five boroughs, we hope New Yorkers and visitors who walk by Links will get a window into the well-known and unsung heroes who have paved the way for women today.\xe2\x80\x9d\nAmong those heroes are Alva Belmont, founder of the Political Equality Association in New York, journalist and civic activist Bessye Bearden, Elizabeth Cady Stanton, who was a drafter of the Declaration of Sentiments, suffrage leader Mabel Lee and Sarah J.S. Tompkins Garnet, who founded the Equal Suffrage League in Brooklyn.\nThe museum\xe2\x80\x99s exhibit features photos, audio materials, garments and more to tell the stories of the city\xe2\x80\x99s female activists, and DoITTT Commissioner Samir Saini hopes that its partnership with LinkNYC \xe2\x80\x9cwill inspire activism among all the people \xe2\x80\x94 male and female \xe2\x80\x94 of our city today,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\nWhitney Donhauser, president of the Museum of City of New York, called the collaboration a "perfect match" that "will bring the story of women\xe2\x80\x99s activism in New York to life in unprecedented ways and make the inspiring history of \xe2\x80\x98Beyond Suffrage\xe2\x80\x99 accessible for even more New Yorkers, tourists and visitors.\xe2\x80\x9d\nMore than 1,300 LinkNYC kiosks can be found across the five boroughs, and thousands more will be deployed in the coming years.\nTags:WomenWomen\'s History MonthNew York City\nLoading...\nLatest From city\nVegan Dominican food comes to the South Bronx\nHealth Pulse Extra\nSubscribe to Health Pulse\nHealth Pulse Pro Corporate Membership\nPhoto Galleries\nSNAPS\nSponsored Photo Galleries\nVideos\nMENU\nBreadcrumb\nHome\nTechnology\nFebruary 06, 2018 11:00 PM\nThe Winter Olympics is coming to LinkNYC\nMatthew Flamm\nTweet\nShare\nShare\nEmail\nMore\nPrint\nIntersection\nIn a first for the digital billboard industry, highlights from the Winter Olympics will appear on the more than 1,500 Wi-Fi hubs that are replacing pay phone kiosks citywide as part of the LinkNYC network.\nFrom Feb. 9 through the closing ceremony Feb. 25, LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s digital screens will post morning highlights, prime-time previews, medal counts and athlete profiles from the games in Pyeongchang, South Korea, throughout the day.\nFor NBC, which has never distributed its Olympic programming via the out-of-home advertising space, the deal marks the latest effort to extend the games\xe2\x80\x99 reach across an increasingly fragmented audience. LinkNYC, meanwhile, gets to showcase new programming and collect data on how audiences on the street interact with the content.\nFrom there, LinkNYC can develop a more tailored pitch for advertisers that might range from the store right beside the kiosk to a national brand looking to do a citywide takeover.\nThe product of a public-private partnership, LinkNYC has an\xc2\xa0ad revenue-sharing arrangement\xc2\xa0with the city that requires it to deliver $500 million during the first 12 years of the agreement. The deal with NBC\xe2\x80\x99s Olympics division will also bring the customized content to digital networks in Chicago and Philadelphia operated by Intersection.\nAccording to Intersection CEO Ari Buchalter, there will be more programming partnerships of this kind.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re talking to a large number of folks that have unique and engaging content, whether that\xe2\x80\x99s news, entertainment, sports or local stories, so we can test and experiment [and see] what content people want to experience in that setting,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd then we can see what is the best way\xe2\x80\x9d for advertisers to sponsor the content people want to see and develop strategies related to it.\nNBC\xe2\x80\x99s programming also could reintroduce LinkNYC to New Yorkers who know of it chiefly as the Wi-Fi hub that, for a period in 2016, attracted users who watched pornography on its interactive tablet. The company solved that problem by disabling the tablet\xe2\x80\x99s web browser.\nRelated Articles\nHBO surpasses 5 million U.S. online subscribers\nPrince's former manager Londell McMillan explains Jay-Z's beef with him\nDolan, Garden keeping WNBA's Liberty for now\nUnlimited-movie deal could be too good to survive\nSale of Harvey Weinstein's company up in air after lawsuit\nFilm and TV parking workers vote to unionize\nA relaunch for Gothamist, but not for DNAinfo\nView the discussion thread.\nGet our newsletters\nStaying current is easy with Crain's New York news delivered straight to your inbox, free of charge\nEmail Address\nCrain's Student Offer\nWe offer a discounted rate through Student Beans for students with a valid .edu email address.
