JOBSFind a JobPost a JobCURRENT OFFERUnlimited Job Postings My Account Log Out Sign In Subscribe\nEmerging TechNBC Will Show Winter Olympics Content on 4,000 Outdoor Displays in 3 U.S. CitiesIntersection brings the games to New York, Chicago and PhiladelphiaBy Marty Swant|February 6, 2018\nA mock-up of a LinkNYC kiosk that will display Winter Olympics content. They will begin showing content on Thursday.IntersectionShareBy Marty Swant|February 6, 2018\nShareOlympics fans in New York, Chicago and Philadelphia will soon have a way to catch up with the 2018 Winter Olympics without looking down at their phones during their commute.Later this week, NBC Olympics will begin showcasing content from\xc2\xa0Pyeongchang, South Korea\xe2\x80\x94videos and visuals such as highlights, summaries, previews, medal counts and athlete bios\xe2\x80\x94on digital displays on streets and in mass transit systems in those three cities. Through a partnership with Intersection, a New York-based smart cities and media company, NBC hopes to broaden its Olympics footprint while reminding people to watch the games on TV or on NBC\xe2\x80\x99s mobile app.According to\xc2\xa0NBC Olympics President Gary Zenkel, the goal is to reach viewers beyond their usual consumption habits. Since there is a 14-hour time difference between the East Coast and South Korea, Zenkel said he hopes it will also provide ongoing content even though the games are half a world away. That means having highlights from the night before during the morning commute in the U.S. to show people what happened while they were still sleeping.\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a real-time presence of Olympic content that\xe2\x80\x99s accompanying people who are either heading to work or doing what they do as they maneuver the streets of New York, Philly and Chicago,\xe2\x80\x9d he told Adweek during an interview from South Korea.Starting Thursday, around 4,000 digital displays will begin showing Olympics content for about three to six minutes every hour. The New York City monoliths stand 9.5 feet tall, and have 55-inch display screens. Zenkel said the goal is to increase the \xe2\x80\x9cappetite\xe2\x80\x9d for Olympics content.The idea came about a couple of months ago after Zenkel noticed the LinkNYC stands around New York. Soon after that, Zenkel ran into Intersection chief revenue officer Marta Martinez and decided to contact her later to learn more about the displays.\xe2\x80\x9cI saw these kiosks popping up on what felt like at least every city block and in some cases corners and was intrigued,\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0Zenkel said.This is the first major content play for Intersection, which has digital display partnerships with a number of major cities in the U.S. Screens can show all kinds of content, including ads like Apple\xe2\x80\x99s Shark Tank-style show, \xe2\x80\x9cPlanet of the Apps,\xe2\x80\x9d as well as offer free Wi-Fi. Other Intersection markets include Dallas, San Francisco, Seattle, Minneapolis and most recently Los Angeles.The Olympics content will be displayed across the 1,300 LinkNYC kiosks in New York; on digital panels and displays in the Chicago Transit Authority system; and on bus shelters, urban panels and other displays in Philadelphia\xe2\x80\x99s mass transit system and streets.\xe2\x80\x9cIt ties back to our core mission, which is to improve [the] daily life of cities through technology,\xe2\x80\x9d said Intersection CEO Ari Buchalter. \xe2\x80\x9cI think a big part of that is around delivering unique and powerful content experiences in the public space, in particular those that are sort of human-scale, look-up experiences as opposed to the content that people often consume on their mobile phones.\xe2\x80\x9dThe initial plan late last year was to find advertisers among NBC\xe2\x80\x99s existing content sponsors. However, Zenkel said the plan came together just before the games were set to begin, and the two companies decided not to exchange any money\xe2\x80\x94unless they\xe2\x80\x99re able to find an advertiser at the last minute.\xe2\x80\x9cThe Olympics is a uniquely massive event,\xe2\x80\x9d Zenkel said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think anyone who walks down the street seeing some great Olympic content is going to say, \xe2\x80\x98Hmm, how did this end up here?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9dBuchalter said Intersection is also in talks to bring other types of content to public spaces. That might include news, social media, local info or cultural content. Buchalter said revenue agreements depend on each contract. However, the share with LinkNYC, a joint partnership with New York City, is split in half.\xe2\x80\x9cIf you only see an ad, then you eventually become blind to that space,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. JOBSFind a JobPost a JobCURRENT OFFERUnlimited Job Postings My Account Log Out Sign In Subscribe\nBrand MarketingThese Out-of-Home Avengers Ads Displayed Showtimes at the Closest Theater to YouCampaign took over 700 LinkNYC kiosksBy Kristina Monllos|May 1, 2018\nThe ads featured an integration with Moviefone, using their proprietary API, to pull in the closest theater location to the kiosk.Courtesy of IntersectionShareBy Kristina Monllos|May 1, 2018\nShareIf you\xe2\x80\x99re a Marvel fan excited to see Avengers: Infinity War opening weekend you\xe2\x80\x99ve likely planned that out in advance\xe2\x80\x94especially if you\xe2\x80\x99re in New York, as theaters sell out quickly here.But what about the casual moviegoer who isn\xe2\x80\x99t as clued into the ins and outs of the Marvel Universe? Disney and Marvel worked with technology and media company Intersection to create a first of its kind out-of-home campaign that used roughly 1400 screens or 700 LinkNYC kiosks\xe2\x80\x94all of the kiosks below 125th street\xe2\x80\x94to make sure consumers were aware of the film, its showtimes and the closest theater.\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s actually an enormous amount of digital displays,\xe2\x80\x9d explained\xc2\xa0Dave Etherington, chief strategy officer at Intersection. \xe2\x80\x9cLinkNYC itself is the largest employment of digital displays in any city in the world so to be able to take the lion\xe2\x80\x99s share of these is pretty significant. The campaign itself was designed to drive awareness as well as ticket sales and theater visits.\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0The campaign kicked off last Thursday evening between 5 p.m. and 7 p.m. with ads that read, \xe2\x80\x9cSee it tonight,\xe2\x80\x9d and featured the Avengers\xe2\x80\x99 logo. The next day the ads featured an integration with Moviefone, using their proprietary API, to pull in the closest theater location to the kiosk the ad appeared on as well as the next showtime for the film so that passerby, if inspired by the ad, could easily catch the next showing.\xe2\x80\x9cOnce you\xe2\x80\x99re exposed to the creative you see the nearest theater playing and a countdown clock to the next movie screening,\xe2\x80\x9d said Etherington, who added that the geographically targeted ads work as \xe2\x80\x9ca call to action.\xe2\x80\x9d\nSharehttp://adweek.it/2HKU4FZ copy Kristina Monllos@KristinaMonllosKristina Monllos is a senior editor for Adweek.Popular Now1 Nike\xe2\x80\x99s Air Force 1 Low Puerto Rico Shoes Illustrated a Lack of Cultural Competency2 Retargeting: Here\xe2\x80\x99s Why Products Seem to Follow You on Social3 Taco Bell Reveals the First Photos of Its Palm Springs Resort\xe2\x80\x94and They\xe2\x80\x99re Very on Brand4 The 25 Best Ads of 20185 Walmart Associates Want $15 Per Hour. All Rights ReservedAbout AdweekContact UsTerms of UsePrivacy Policy", b'LinkNYC delivers better quality of life with digital signage, Wi-Fi | Digital Signage TodayTest LinkCONTINUE TO SITE \xc2\xbb or wait 15 seconds\xc3\x97Toggle navigation\nTOPICS 3D Digital Signage4K Ultra HDAdvertisingAudience MeasurementBanks / FinancialCellular SignageCloud-Based Digital SignageContentContent ManagementCorporate CommunicationCustomer ExperienceDigital BillboardsDisplay TechnologyDistributors / ResellersDOOH AdvertisingEducation / SchoolsEntertainment VenuesHardwareHealthcare / HospitalsHotelsInstallation / IntegrationInteractive / TouchscreenLED SignsMenu BoardsMobile InteractivityOutdoor SignageRestaurantsRetailSoftwareTrends / StatisticsWayfindingView all Topic Centers \xc2\xbbSUPPLIERS Companies by NameCompanies by CategoryProducts & ServicesRequest Information from SuppliersPROJECT HELPRESOURCESNEWSWEBINARSEVENTS View Industry Event Calendar >>MORE VideosWebinarsEventsPodcastsPhotosArticlesVideosBlogsPress ReleasesJob ListingsProject HelpMedia Kit / Editorial CalendarBloggersStore\nGet the latest news & insightsSubscribe\nLinkNYC delivers better quality of life with digital signage, Wi-FiJune 22, 2018 | by Bradley CooperIn 2016, New York City went through a major smart city upgrade, as Intersection deployed multiple Link kiosks. The city replaced older phone booths with these kiosks, which offer free Wi-Fi to the public, as well as advertising and wayfinding.The kiosks also allow customers to make free nationwide calls, or report emergencies. There are now more than 1,600 kiosks in all five boroughs of the city. Digital Signage Today spoke with Ruth Fasoldt, director of community affairs for Link, to see how these devices are transforming the city and improving lives.Q. What are the main features the kiosks offer?A. LinkNYC is the first-of-its-kind communications network replacing the city\'s payphones to build the world\'s fastest and largest free public Wi-Fi network. Since Mayor Bill de Blasio announced the public launch of LinkNYC in early 2016, more than 1,600 Links are active across all five boroughs, with thousands more set to be deployed over the next several years.In addition to free Wi-Fi, Links offer free nationwide phone calls, a dedicated 911 button, device charging, and a tablet to access maps and city services. Link\'s services come at no cost to users or taxpayers because Link generates its own revenue through advertising on the 55-inch digital displays on the sides of kiosks.Q. How do they improve the lives of residents?A. LinkNYC provides so many benefits to New Yorkers and visitors. More than 4 million people \xe2\x80\x94 more than the populations of the cities of Chicago, Phoenix, Philadelphia, Dallas\xc2\xa0or San Diego \xe2\x80\x94 have used the free gigabit Wi-Fi service, with tens of thousands of users joining the network each week. The network also sees more than 250,000 free phone calls made every month. Using the tablet, people can access maps and directions on the go.Along with ads that keep LinkNYC\'s services 100 percent free for users and taxpayers, the digital displays feature useful and enriching content, including community board meeting updates, real-time transit and weather information so people can make more informed decisions about their day on the go, PSAs, fun facts about NYC, historic photos\xc2\xa0and more. The screens are also used for emergency messaging, for instance, in an extreme weather event. We see tweets and Instagram posts all the time of people capturing our content and sharing it with others.Q. How does LinkNYC deal with issues such as people loitering by the kiosks or watching inappropriate content in public?A. Back in 2016, there was an issue with some kiosks having long-term users. The LinkNYC tablet is meant to be an on-the-go resource, so the web browser was removed from Link tablets in September 2016, in exchange for curated content on the tablet, and loitering complaints dropped 96 percent immediately.Q. What type of ads do the kiosks display?A. LinkNYC has a very high caliber of advertisers across categories \xe2\x80\x94 from Samsung to Delta to The Gap and The Met.Utilizing DOOH\xc2\xa0to its fullest and breaking from the norm of basic, static ads, Link kiosks offer the ability for advertisers to display unique, dynamic ads. From weather and transit, to sporting events, movie times and more, Link ads can change based on real-time information and updates, keeping advertisements relevant and consumers engaged.During the 2018 Winter Olympics in PeyongChang, for example, NBC partnered with Intersection to display Olympics content and coverage on LinkNYC screens, highlights, prime time previews, real-time medal counts, athlete bios and more. This digital OOH content campaign was the first of its kind for the U.S. Olympics broadcaster.More recently, Intersection pioneered another first-of-its-kind campaign, partnering with Disney and Marvel to promote "The Avengers: Infinity War." On the movie\'s launch weekend, LinkNYC screens displayed ads for the blockbuster, as well as the closest theater location to each kiosk and the next show time, so that passersby, if inspired by the ad, could easily catch the next showing.Q. Do the kiosks use any analytics?A. We have stats on usership, how often different services are used, the busiest Links and more. We have also made strategic use of our network capabilities like dayparting (for example, we increase transit info on our displays during peak commuting hours), geotargeting (playing historical photos in their place of original capture), and network flexibility (during Women\'s History month, we displayed facts about women\'s suffrage along the route of the women\'s march).Q. Do you think smart cities will start to pop up everywhere? Why?A.\xc2\xa0Cities around the world are looking for ways to better deliver services to residents and visitors, increase broadband connectivity, and adapt to the needs of the digital age. Many are looking to New York and LinkNYC in particular as a model. In addition to New York, a Link network is live in the U.K.\xc2\xa0We have planned expansions into Philadelphia and Newark, with many more cities on the way.Image via Link.Topics: Advertising, Audience Measurement, Content, Customer Experience, Display Technology, DOOH Advertising, Outdoor Signage Bradley CooperBradley Cooper is a Technology Editor for DigitalSignageToday.com and BlockchainTechNews.com. Images will be displayed from the Museum\xe2\x80\x99s current exhibition, Through a Different Lens: Stanley Kubrick Photographs.\nPasserby on the street will be able to catch a glimpse of the old New York through the lens of the iconic film director. Kubrick\xe2\x80\x99s photographs highlight his formative years as a photographer (before he became a film director) for Look magazine in New York City between 1945-1950. The photographs focus on and capture the pathos of everyday life of the city, from street scenes to sporting events.\nThe LinkNYC kiosks can be found dotted all over the city. Since Mayor Bill de Blasio launched the program in 2016, more than 1,650 Links are active across all five boroughs and have replaced the old pay phones with sleek kiosks that feature free Wi-Fi, phone chargers, and digital displays for advertisements and in this case, art.\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not the first time that LinkNYC has featured art on its kiosks from MCNY. Previous \xe2\x80\x9cexhibitions\xe2\x80\x9d on the kiosks include historic photos of women who influenced New York\xe2\x80\x99s political history for Women\xe2\x80\x99s History Month and \xe2\x80\x9cOn This Day in NYC History\xe2\x80\x9d information. The MCNY and LinkNYC partnership is one of many programs that disseminate New York City\xe2\x80\x99s history; others include the NYC Space/Time Directory from the New York Public Library, an app from Urban Archive that made more than 2,500 images of old New York available on-the-go, and a Civil Rights & Social Justice Map from the Greenwich Village Society.\nLinkNYC\nMCNY\nPublic Art\nRelated Dive\nCONTINUE TO SITE \xe2\x9e\x9e\nDeep Dive\nOpinion\nLibrary\nEvents\nJobs\nTopics\nMenu\nSign Up\nSearch\nSearch\nx\nEnergy & Utilities\nTransportation\nBuildings & Infrastructure\nEnvironment\nResilience\nGovernance\nTech & Data\nAn article from\nHow TransitScreen helps city dwellers preserve a valuable asset: time\nCEO and Co-founder Matt Caywood said by curating transit information, people can make better and more efficient mobility decisions.\nAuthor\nBy\nKristin Musulin\n@kristinmusulin\nPublished\nJune 21, 2018\nShare it\npost\nshare\ntweet\nTen years ago, in the neuroscience lab at the University of California, San Francisco, a graduate student was developing experiments involving an unlikely interest: transportation.\nMatt Caywood, a Chicago native, was always fascinated by public transit. He had previously built himself a trip planner for London Underground (a good four years prior to London launching its own planner), and at UCSF, he built his own tools to determine the most efficient transit options home after late nights of studying. This passion for tech-driven mobility solutions led Caywood to Washington, DC, where his infatuation with transportation transformed into a business.\nIn 2013, Caywood and co-founder Ryan Croft launched TransitScreen, a company that curates local, real-time mobility information \xe2\x80\x94 including bus and rail times, wait times for ride-sharing apps and the proximity of bike- and scooter-share systems \xe2\x80\x94 and displays it on screens in commercial buildings. The screens are located across more than 40 cities in the U.S. and Canada, with some even sprinkled throughout the U.K., Ireland and France.\nThe growth of TransitScreen followed a true startup trajectory, having started in Caywood\'s garage before moving to the former 1776 incubator, and eventually into its own office. Caywood describes the company as "scrappy" and touts its most strategic business decision \xe2\x80\x94\xc2\xa0to sell to real estate clients.\nThe TransitScreen office in Washington, DC.\nKristin Musulin\n"The cities are advocates for us because we\xe2\x80\x99re helping them by providing public information that anyone, no matter who they are \xe2\x80\x94 young or old, rich or poor \xe2\x80\x94 can get,"\xc2\xa0Caywood said. "But what we do instead is work with the real estate industry and with employers to put that information into as many public and public-ish locations as possible."\nTransitScreen displays are most commonly found in commercial offices, apartment buildings, hotels, restaurants and university buildings.\n"It\'s a very different model from, say, a LinkNYC model where they have to spend hundreds of millions in capital costs to roll out their network then find a way to recoup that," Caywood explained. "We\'re able to make a very large impact on smart cities while still being a very small and lightly-funded company."\nReal-time data on the big screen\nBy offering transportation information on a public display, the TransitScreen team is aiming to preserve a valued asset of the everyday public transit user: time.\nA recent report from McKinsey Global Institute\xc2\xa0found that, by 2025, the cities that deploy smart mobility applications could reduce average commuting times by 15-20%. "When a resident looks at real-time traffic data and decides to set out at a less busy time, she avoids adding another car to the road that would worsen congestion for everyone," the report says.\xc2\xa0"Millions of individual decisions and actions add up, making the city as a whole more productive and responsive."\nTransitScreen\nCaywood said by giving city residents the option to view this real-time data right before walking out of the door, it alleviates the responsibility of looking up the information on your mobile device. And, while TransitScreen has optimized its service to be responsive to a mobile screen, Caywood said only one in every 10 public transit riders ever checks their phone for such information.\n"Most of the trips that you\xe2\x80\x99re going to make are starting at a particular location \xe2\x80\x94 your home or your work. Being able to provide the information at a glance in an efficient and easy-to-use manner, that\xe2\x80\x99s when you have the biggest impact," he said.\nOf course the company faces a lot of pressure to keep its information accurate and up-to-date as new mobility solutions enter the market. Caywood said this is a "core goal of our product," and is accomplished through active partnerships.\n"Our approach is we want to work with all of the different mobility providers to inform our audience ... about the options that are available and the choices that they can now make," he said. "So our approach to that has been to partner with them, and we\'re now seeing that as we\'ve established our presence in the space, people are kind of now coming to us with data and saying, \'What does it take to get on TransitScreen\'s platform?\'"\nEven with the influx of new electric scooter and dockless bike companies coming online, Caywood said TransitScreen is in "active conversations" with everyone in the space.\nRanking a location with MobilityScore\nIn addition to the traditional TransitScreen platform, the company has also developed MobilityScore, a tool that ranks city locations based on access to mobility services. Similar to tools like Walk Score, MobilityScore measures how easy it is to move around a city by scoring any location or address from 0 (no mobility options) to 100 (excellent mobility options).\n"It\xe2\x80\x99s based on actual data and not just schedules, so it\xe2\x80\x99s the only tool of its kind,"\xc2\xa0Caywood said. And while the tool is only in its beta phase, it has already been rolled out in most of the top 100 largest cities in North America. The company has also worked with real estates sites like Rent Jungle to optimize property and rental searches.\nCaywood called MobilityScore an "intrinsically international product" and said TransitScreen will continue to roll out the tool in new places.\xc2\xa0In a blog post,\xc2\xa0the company also called the tool "future-proof" and said it will be continuously updated with information on microtransit, autonomous vehicles and mobility-as-a-service.\nThe MobilityScore results for a location in the Dupont Circle neighborhood of Washington, DC.\nTransitScreen\nLooking forward\nFrom its active social media accounts to regular e-mail newsletters, TransitScreen is vocal about its desire to grow alongside the cities where it operates. Caywood hinted the company has a few new offerings in the works, and is continually looking for ways to "make the TransitScreen experience more relevant to the people who are viewing it and using it."\nAnd aside from internal strategies,\xc2\xa0Caywood believes the evolution of smart cities will help the company stay along a successful growth path. He said his understanding of a "smart city" is one that takes data and translates it into useful information \xe2\x80\x94 which is at the core of TransitScreen\'s business.\n"We started with this unique public information solution but we\xe2\x80\x99re really taking it to wherever people are making decisions based on mobility," he said. "There\xe2\x80\x99s a whole different side of smart cities that people don\'t even think about because we\xe2\x80\x99re so caught up in stage one, which is data collection. Stage two is where, say Waze starts changing traffic patterns and you have to start thinking what to do with it. That\xe2\x80\x99s the interesting part and that\xe2\x80\x99s sort of where the future of smart cities is going. So that\xe2\x80\x99s where we\xe2\x80\x99re pointed to.\xe2\x80\x9d\nFollow\nKristin Musulin\non\nTwitter\nshare\ntweet\npost\nemail\nprint\nFiled Under:\nTransportation\nTech & Data\nTop image credit:\nTransitScreen\nGet smart cities news like this in your inbox daily. Pei\xe2\x80\x99s Grand Central-replacing colossus to Buckminster Fuller\xe2\x80\x99s Dodgers Dome in Brooklyn, it\xe2\x80\x99s all in here\nBy\nTanay Warerkar@TanayWarerkar\nJul 10, 2018,\n3:38pm EDT\nShare\nTweet\nShare\nShare\nLinkNYC kiosks will display fantastical, never-built NYC structures\ntweet\nshare\nReddit\nPocket\nFlipboard\nEmail\nVia LinkNYC\nFor its latest campaign, LinkNYC has teamed up with authors Greg Goldin and Sam Lubell to highlight New York structures that were never built. This digital exhibit is a follow up to the release of their book, \xe2\x80\x98Never Built New York,\xe2\x80\x99 which came out in 2016, and their subsequent exhibition at the Queens Museum last fall.\nIn the LinkNYC partnership, these never built projects will be displayed as close as possible to their would be locations in the city. Take for instance I.M. Pei\xe2\x80\x99s Hyperboloid, a 102-story circular tower that would have replaced Grand Central Terminal, and would have been the tallest structure in the world\xe2\x80\x94that will be visible on LinkNYC kiosks near the station.\nOther never built structures that have received recognition on LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s digital billboards include Moshe Safdie\xe2\x80\x99s Habitat New York 1, an origami-like luxury residence and shopping complex proposed to rise north of Gracie Mansion, on the Upper East Side; and the domed stadium designed by Buckminster Fuller, that would have kept the Dodgers in Brooklyn. Peek at some of the others below.\nThis is LinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s latest collaboration following ones with the Museum of the City of New York in March, to honor women activists; and the one with the Department of Records and Information Services (DORIS) last year to show off historic photos of NYC neighborhoods.\nThe New York City transit projects that never were\nHelp bring a \xe2\x80\x98Never Built New York\xe2\x80\x99 exhibit to life at the Queens Museum\nNext Up In\nNews\nNew York Botanical Garden\xe2\x80\x99s stinky corpse flower will bloom soon\nDigital billboards should be banned from NYC waterways: lawmakers\nNew York lawmakers vote to legalize e-bikes, e-scooters\nInfamous landlord to pay $3M in tenant harassment settlement\nNotorious B.I.G.\xe2\x80\x99s childhood home now a $4,000/month rental\nBrooklyn lawmaker wants to resurrect Triboro rail line\nMost Read\nWilliamsburg\xe2\x80\x99s quirky shipping container house lists for $5.5M\nThe home on a corner lot is made up of 21 shipping containers meticulously pieced together\nWhat $1M buys in NYC right now\nFive apartments, five NYC neighborhoods\nLovely Ditmas Park townhouse with a huge pool asks $2M\nThe landmarked Brooklyn home has a ton of "old world charm."\nNotorious B.I.G.\xe2\x80\x99s childhood home now a $4,000/month rental\nThe apartment where the late rapper grew up is up for grabs\nNYC\xe2\x80\x99s 25 most expensive homes for sale\nHere now, check out the 25 most expensive listings in NYC\xe2\x80\x94they\'re just as ridiculously over-the-top as you might expect.\nSign up for the\nCurbed NY Newsletter\nEmail (required)\nSubscribe\nBy signing up, you agree to our Privacy Policy and European users agree to the data transfer policy.\nThis Article has a component height of 33. All Rights Reserved\nNew York\ntweet\nshare', b"LinkNYC brings never-built megaprojects to the streets of New York - Archpaper.com\nLinkNYC brings never-built megaprojects to the streets of New York\nMenu\nAwards\nAdvertise\nSubscribe\nContact\nAbout\nPrivacy Policy\nMap\nEvents\nCompetitions\nProducts\nJobs\nTopics\nRegions\nInternational\nEast\nSoutheast\nMidwest\nWest\nSouthwest\nTopics\nAN Interior\nArchitecture\nArt\nDesign\nDevelopment\nPreservation\nTransportation\nUrbanism\nNewsletters\nFacades+\nSpec Sheet\nCity Terrain\nLate Edition: East\nLate Edition: West\nLate Edition: Midwest\nLate Edition: Southwest\nConferences\nFacades+ Conference\nFacades+ AM\nTech+\nEvents\nCompetitions\nProducts\nJobs\nConferences\nConferences\nFacades+ Conferences\nTech+ Expo\nAwards\nSubscribe\nCall the Mirror Universe\nLinkNYC brings never-built megaprojects to the streets of New York\nBy\nJonathan Hilburg\n(@jhilburg)\n\xe2\x80\xa2\nJuly 13, 2018\nShare:\nNew Yorkers can catch a glimpse of a parallel universe this summer. LinkNYC, the Department of Information Technology & Telecommunications, AN contributor Sam Lubell, writer\xc2\xa0Greg Goldin, and publisher Metropolis Books have teamed up to bring images from Never Built New York to the city\xe2\x80\x99 streets via LinkNYC kiosks.\nThe display of unbuilt megaprojects from some of the biggest names in architecture follows the release of the Never Built New York book in 2016, and the accompanying show at the Queens Museum last fall. The kiosks won\xe2\x80\x99t display the full array of weird and wild never-realized projects, but the curated images will still depict how New York could have grown into a very different city.\nA kiosk display of Howe & Lescaze\xe2\x80\x99s unbuilt Museum of Modern Art. (Courtesy LinkNYC)\nSome of the work on display includes I.M. Pei\xe2\x80\x99s proposal for the Hyperboloid, a 102-story tower proposed in 1954 that would have replaced Grand Central, and Robert Moses\xe2\x80\x99s heavily contested Mid-Manhattan Expressway. Images of the Dodger Dome, an enclosed stadium designed by Buckminster Fuller meant to keep the Dodgers in Brooklyn, and Moshe Safdie\xe2\x80\x99s tessellating Habitat New York (originally slated for the Upper East Side) have also been selected. LinkNYC will display images of each project on kiosks close to the location where they would have risen.\nA kiosk display of William Zeckendorf\xe2\x80\x99s 67-block-long Dream Airport, which would have floated in the Hudson River. (Courtesy LinkNYC)\nLinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s 1,650 kiosks can be found all over the city following the program\xe2\x80\x99s launch in 2016. The Never Built New York\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x98exhibition\xe2\x80\x99 follows a June show that presented historical New York City photos from the Museum of the City of New York\xe2\x80\x99s ongoing Through a Different Lens: Stanley Kubrick Photographs exhibition.\nAbout the author\nJonathan Hilburg\n(@jhilburg)\nWeb Editor, The Architect's Newspaper\nBuckminster Fuller\nI.M. Pei\nLinkNYC\nMoshe Safdie\nNew York City\nRelated Stories\nJune 17, 2019\nColor Blind\nPlaywright Oren Safdie takes on racial tensions of national architecture\nJune 10, 2019\nSchool's In?\nFormer I.M. AutomationCybersecurityCloud & InfrastructureData & AnalyticsSmart Cities & IoTEmerging TechState & LocalMoreEventsResourcesNewslettersContactAdvertiseReprintsList Rental\nNew ways to secure public Wi-Fi\nBy Matt LeonardAug 24, 2018\nCities that want to offer public Wi-Fi are understandably concerned about security.\nConsumer devices automatically log onto networks they\xe2\x80\x99re familiar with, so a bad actor can set up a network with the same name as a city's network and compromise users who sign on. Intersection, the company behind LinkNYC and LinkNWK public Wi-Fi kiosks in New York City and Newark, N.J., is now offering an app to secure connections on its networks.\nThe Link Wi-Fi App will provide an encrypted connection between the device and the network and will ensure that devices don\xe2\x80\x99t connect to other \xe2\x80\x9cevil twin\xe2\x80\x9d networks, which would allow bad actors to steal and view user information, Stacey Levine, the VP of communications at Intersection, told GCN.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe only sure-fire way to avoid these evil-twin networks is to use a secure method of network access such as an app and that\xe2\x80\x99s why we\xe2\x80\x99ve developed this,\xe2\x80\x9d she said of the encrypted app.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe security of public Wi-Fi networks is increasingly an area of focus for cities who want to protect their residents and visitors from hackers, imposter networks and other threats that can compromise or steal user data, often without users even realizing it,\xe2\x80\x9d Intersection President Jen Hensley said. \xe2\x80\x9cUnlike many public wifi networks, the LinkNWK network will ensure a secure, encrypted connection for all Apple and Android phones through the Link Wi-Fi app.\xe2\x80\x9d\nLinkNWK will be the first city to have the app when it activates its 45 kiosks later this fall, Levine said.\nLinkNYC has both a public and private network. LinkNYC Private requires downloading a Hotspot 2.0 profile that enables encryption and automatically connects users from one hotspot to the next without requiring them to log in to each new network. It also recently signed a deal with Quad9 to secure its guest and free public Wi-Fi networks by blocking access to known malicious sites.\nLink Wi-Fi App will instead be downloaded like any standard smartphone app, a process users are more familiar with, Levine said, and it will be available for iOS and Android users.\nThe app will automatically connect a device to the LinkNWK network any time it is within range. It will also provide a map of nearby active kiosks. Future updates could provide the ability to access information similar to what people can see on the kiosks themselves -- including events, city information and transit updates.\nThis app will also give Intersection data for monitoring internet connectivity. Analysts will be able to see when people have trouble connecting and if the problem is due to a specific operating system or device, which will help the service to troubleshoot, Levine said.\nLinkNWK taps into Newark's fiber network for internet connectivity. For LinkNYC, Intersection has invested in a \xc2\xa0purpose-built fiber optic network for gigabit connectivity.\nThe company also is in talks with the other cities with Link kiosks about rolling out this app to those locations, Levine said.\n\xe2\x80\x9cFundamentally,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cconnectivity is kind of like the basis of smart city technology. Things need to be connected, people need access to communication, so we think this is a foundational piece of their smart city efforts.\xe2\x80\x9d\nAbout the Author\nMatt Leonard is a former reporter for GCN.\nE-Mail this page\nPrintable Format\nRelated Articles\nWhite House takes on cyber workforce gap\nStop chasing ghosts and build a threat hunting strategy\nMoving IT security from human to For example, did you know 52% of NYC businesses are immigrant-owned, or that nearly half of the city\xe2\x80\x99s population speaks a language other than English at home?\nRuth Fasoldt, Link\xe2\x80\x99s Director of Community Affairs, said in a statement: \xe2\x80\x9cNew York City is a city of immigrants, and we are thrilled to use the Link network to highlight their important contributions to city life. Through bringing facts and photography about our history to the streets of New York, we hope to inspire pride in our city\xe2\x80\x99s diversity, our heritage, and our neighbors.\xe2\x80\x9d\nSome of the facts that will be on display include:\n52% of NYC businesses are immigrant-owned\nThe top countries of origin for NYC immigrants are the Dominican Republic, China, Mexico, Jamaica, and Guyana\nNYC is home to 3.1 million immigrants, the largest number in city history\nImmigrants make up nearly 38% of the NYC population and 45% of the city\xe2\x80\x99s workforce\n49% all New Yorkers speak a language other than English at home\nImmigrants contributed an estimated $195 billion to NYC\xe2\x80\x99s GDP in 2017\nSince Mayor de Blasio launched LinkNYC in 2016, more than 1,700 kiosks have been activated across all five boroughs. Please try again later.", b"LinkNYC's 5 million users make 500,000 phone calls each month | VentureBeat\nCHANNELS l\nl\nCHANNELS\nGamesBeat\nAI\nAR/VR\nBig Lab\nEVENTS l\nl\nVB EVENTS\nUpcoming Events\nGET INVOLVED\nSponsor\nMedia Partner\nVolunteer\nGot a news tip?\nPress Releases\nWebinars\nAdvertise\nVB Lab\nNEWSLETTERS\nJOB BOARD\n\xe2\x80\xb9\nCHANNELS\n\xe2\x80\xba\nCHANNELS\nGamesBeat\nEntrepreneur\nAI\nEsports\nAR/VR\nMarketing\nBig Data\nMedia\nBusiness\nMobile\nCloud\nPC Gaming\nCommerce\nSecurity\nDev\nSocial\nEnterprise\nTransportation\n\xe2\x80\xb9\nEVENTS\n\xe2\x80\xba\nVB EVENTS\nUpcoming Events\nGET INVOLVED\nSponsor\nMedia Partner\nVolunteer\nNEWSLETTERS\nJOB BOARD\n\xe2\x80\xb9\nVENTUREBEAT\n\xe2\x80\xba\nAbout\nAdvertise\nCareers\nContact\nGot a news tip?\nPress Releases\nVB Lab\nWebinars\nPrivacy Policy\nMOBILE\nLinkNYC\xe2\x80\x99s 5 million users make 500,000 phone calls each month\nKyle Wiggers@Kyle_L_Wiggers September 29, 2018 4:15 AM\nImage Credit: LinkNYC\nMOST READ\n6 things your boss doesn\xe2\x80\x99t know about software development\nAdam Cheyer: Samsung\xe2\x80\x99s plan for winning with Bixby is empowering third-party developers\nUiPath: RPA and AI will be commoditized productivity tools within 5 years\nCloudflare launches free time service with Network Time Security support\nProBeat: Tablets were always doomed\nIn 2014, in a bid to replace the more than 11,000 aging payphones scattered across New York City\xe2\x80\x99s pedestrian walkways with more functional fixtures, Mayor Bill de Blasio launched a competition \xe2\x80\x94 the Reinvent Payphones initiative \xe2\x80\x94 calling on private enterprises, residents, and nonprofits to submit designs for replacements.\nIn the end, LinkNYC \xe2\x80\x94 a plan proposed by consortium CityBridge \xe2\x80\x94 secured a contract from the city, beating out competing proposals with electricity-generating piezoelectric pressure plates and EV charging stations. The plan was to spend $200 million installing as many as 10,000 kiosks, or Links, that would supply free, encrypted gigabit Wi-Fi to passers-by within 150 feet. They would have buttons that link directly to 911 and New York\xe2\x80\x99s 311 service and free USB charging stations for smartphones, plus wired handsets that would allow free calls to all 50 states and Washington, D.C. And perhaps best of all, they wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t cost the city a dime; advertising would subsidize expansion and ongoing maintenance.\nThe\xc2\xa0Links wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t just get urbanites\xc2\xa0online and let them juice their phones, though. The idea was to engage users, too, principally with twin 55-inch high-definition displays and tethered Android tablets with map functions. Mike Gamaroff, head of innovation at Kinetic, characterized the Links in 2016 as \xe2\x80\x9cfirst and foremost a utility for the people of the city, that also doubles up as an advertising network.\xe2\x80\x9d\nTwo years after the deployment of prototypical kiosks in Manhattan, Intersection \xe2\x80\x94 a part of the aforementioned CityBridge, which with Qualcomm and CIVIQ Smartscapes manages the kiosks \xe2\x80\x94 is ready to declare them a success. The roughly 1,600 Links recently hit three milestones: 1 billion sessions, 5 million users, and 500,000 phone calls a month.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have an opportunity to communicate with people as they navigate their day,\xe2\x80\x9d Intersection senior consumer marketing manager Amanda Giddon told VentureBeat in a phone interview. \xe2\x80\x9cMy mandate is to help make Link a part of the community through content and content strategy \xe2\x80\x94 really, anything that [makes] New Yorkers feel like tourists in their own city [or] even help tourists feel like New Yorkers through useful, actionable information.\xe2\x80\x9d\nCreative content\nAt any given time, the Link kiosks\xe2\x80\x99 screens host news headlines from the Associated Press, comics, weather info, real-time alerts from the Office of Emergency Management, and creative from a mix of roughly 50 other campaigns. Also on tap are hundreds of hyperlocal factoids\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 dubbed \xe2\x80\x9cNYC Fun Facts\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cThis Day in New York\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 about people (\xe2\x80\x9cMartin Hildebrandt opened the United States\xe2\x80\x99 first tattoo business in New York City in 1870\xe2\x80\x9d), places (\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a superhero supply store in Brooklyn\xe2\x80\x9d), and things (\xe2\x80\x9cNew York City gets 15 times more snow than the South Pole each year\xe2\x80\x9d). There are close to 400 trivia tidbits in all, with new ones joining the collection each week.\nGibbon researches the facts herself, typically spending a few hours a week\xc2\xa0poring through a range of sources, including Broadway.org, Grow NYC, Time Magazine, FiveThirtyEight, and the\xc2\xa0National History Museum. She dutifully fact-checks them and copies them to a master spreadsheet before deciding which ones will make the cut.\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been really great to see people writing in about the content they see.\xc2\xa0We\xe2\x80\x99ve created some moments of awe for people, and if I can create a moment of awe for someone on a daily basis, then I\xe2\x80\x99m doing my job right,\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0Giddon said.\nWhen the kiosks aren\xe2\x80\x99t alerting pedestrians to, say, the percentage of New Yorkers riding elevators at any time, they display real-time bus arrivals and local maps. But the bulk of their programming consists of rotating regular, seasonal, and limited-time content collaborations with organizations, publications, and government agencies.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe survey our users quite frequently [for ideas] \xe2\x80\xa6 and we go to great lengths to make sure our [content] is contextually relevant,\xe2\x80\x9d said Giddon. \xe2\x80\x9c[We\xe2\x80\x99re] pioneering this publishing approach and public space and are really eager to get feedback and adjust as we continue to expand.\xe2\x80\x9d\nOne recent example is a partnership with the Department of Information Technology and Telecommunications (DoITT) that showcased the work of local artists. Another is \xe2\x80\x9cPopular Places Near You,\xe2\x80\x9d a Foursquare-powered feature that shows top restaurants and entertainment hubs within walking distance.\nThat\xe2\x80\x99s just the tip of the iceberg. Intersection worked with the Museum of the City of New York\xe2\x80\x99s Beyond Suffrage exhibit to feature NYC women in politics, with the NYC Department of Records to curate historical photography (localized at a neighborhood level), and with Silicon Harlem and Global Kids to showcase legendary\xc2\xa0African Americans\xc2\xa0during Black History Month.\nSocial services\nIntersection\xe2\x80\x99s\xc2\xa0also leveraging the kiosks to promote civic engagement.\nIn April, it teamed up with the New York City Council to roll out Participatory Budgeting New York City, which let residents as young as 11 vote via the kiosk tablets on how the city will allocate its $40 million public budget. And it launched an awareness campaign to get New Yorkers registered to vote in advance of the November 2018 general elections. (The latter integrated with the city\xe2\x80\x99s voter registration data to show a real-time count of the number of people signed up.) It also posts Community Board meeting notices and local road closures and through its LinkLocal program lets small businesses advertise for free on select kiosks around the city.\nIntersection has experimented with social services, too. In January, users were able to browse and enroll in health plans through New York State of Health insurance marketplace.\nFor some New Yorkers, the Link hubs aren\xe2\x80\x99t just a convenience \xe2\x80\x94 they\xe2\x80\x99re a lifeline. A 2014 study by the Office of the New York City Comptroller found that 27 percent of NYC residents surveyed \xe2\x80\x94 40 percent of whom had less than a high school education \xe2\x80\x94 lacked broadband internet at home.\nWithout a reliable internet connection, students can\xe2\x80\x99t access online classroom resources, out-of-work adults can\xe2\x80\x99t submit job applications, and families struggling to make ends meet can\xe2\x80\x99t take advantage of social services. As the New York Times wrote in August 2016:\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x9cIn urban areas, rural areas, and everywhere in between, students who lack internet service at home have difficulty doing their nightly schoolwork. Many of them cobble together whatever connectivity they can, picking up free Wi-Fi signals in front of libraries, in school parking lots, and at fast-food restaurants.\xe2\x80\x9d\nFour years ago, De Blasio\xc2\xa0touted the Links as a sign of progress in the fight for unimpeded internet access. \xe2\x80\x9c[They\xe2\x80\x99re] the fastest and largest municipal Wi-Fi network in the world,\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0he said, \xe2\x80\x9c[and] a critical step toward a more equal, open, and connected city for every New Yorker, in every borough.\xe2\x80\x9d\nControversy\nBut the accolades tend to ignore the fact that LinkNYC isn\xe2\x80\x99t strictly a philanthropic effort. Advertisements that run alongside Intersection\xe2\x80\x99s programming were expected to generate between $500 million and a billion dollars over the next 12 years. (CityBridge and the city split the ad revenue equally.)\nAnd the kiosks themselves aren\xe2\x80\x99t without controversy.\nThe connected tablets initially had an internet browser, but Intersection disabled it in response to complaints about users browsing pornographic material. It also added vision-assistance tools after the National Federation of the Blind sued the City of New York and LinkNYC, arguing that the tablets lacked basic accessibility features.\nRevenue, meanwhile, has missed expectations.\xc2\xa0Over the first two years, the city collected $43.4 million in payments, narrowly beating the $42.5 million minimum CityBridge guaranteed. Under an amended deal, CityBridge will delay paying the city its share of revenues (above the minimum payments) until the last year of the contract, when they\xe2\x80\x99ll be due with 10 percent interest.\nAnd as The Intercept recently pointed out, consumer advocacy groups and activists, including the American Civil Liberties Union, Electronic Frontier Foundation, Stop LinkNYC, and ReThink LinkNYC, have brought attention to the hubs\xe2\x80\x99 potential for mass surveillance.\nEach hub is equipped with three cameras and sensors capable of, among other things, \xe2\x80\x9cmonitor[ing] pedestrian, bike, and car traffic; track[ing] passing wireless devices; listen[ing] to street noise; and \xe2\x80\xa6 identify[ing] abandoned packages.\xe2\x80\x9d\nNone of this has scared away investors, who extended $150 million in financing to Intersection last year.\nIntersection makes clear in its privacy policy that it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t collect information about users\xe2\x80\x99 precise locations. And in response to recent allegations that it intends to track Wi-Fi users\xe2\x80\x99 real-time positions, it said it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t\xc2\xa0collect their clickstream data or browsing history.\nAs Intersection and CityBridge eye expansion to new markets, Giddon said, they\xe2\x80\x99ll take into account feedback they\xe2\x80\x99ve received so far.\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99ll definitely be a combination of lessons learned and ensuring we add a little local flavor [to our programing],\xe2\x80\x9d Giddon said.\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x9cWe have research teams in New York and Philadelphia who\xe2\x80\x99ve conducted some preliminary focus group testing to understand how to best serve the community. We\xe2\x80\x99re really open to feedback, and we\xe2\x80\x99ve done a lot of work here and look forward to seeing how it\xe2\x80\x99s received.\nIntersection hopes to install 7,500 Link kiosks by 2026, when its contract with the city expires. In June, it launched InLinkUK, a partnership with telecom provider BT and outdoor advertising agency Primesight to replace over 1,000 pay phones in major U.K. cities with kiosks. In September, 100 kiosks\xc2\xa0hit the sidewalks of Philadelphia as part of its LinkPHL program. And by the end of this year, 45 will come to Newark.", b"NYC will roll out thousands more kiosks offering free public Wi-Fi\nGo to the content\nGo to the footer\nClose\nNew York\nChange city\nNew York\n(en)\nEnglish\nEspa\xc3\xb1ol\nPopular cities\nLondon\nNew York\nParis\nChicago\nLos Angeles\nLisbon\nHong Kong\nSydney\nMelbourne\nPorto\nSingapore\nBarcelona\nMadrid\nGirona\nBrowse all cities\nTickets\nEvents\nThings to Do\nTime Out Market\nRestaurants\nBars\nMovies\nTheater\nKids\nArt\nNews\nAttractions\nVideo\nHotels\nTravel\nMusic\nTO Book\nClasses\nMuseums\nShopping\nNightlife\nComedy\nDance\nLGBT\nSex & Dating\nBooks\nCity Guide\nNeighborhoods\nMagazine\nSweepstakes\nVenue Rental\nTime Out New York\nNew York\nEnglish\nEspa\xc3\xb1ol\nPopular cities\nLondon\nNew York\nParis\nChicago\nLos Angeles\nLisbon\nHong Kong\nSydney\nMelbourne\nPorto\nSingapore\nBarcelona\nMadrid\nGirona\nBrowse all cities\nSubscribe\nLove Time Out?\nGet the best of your city in our newsletter, as often as you like\nD\xc3\xa9j\xc3\xa0 vu! Brought to you by Microsoft\nPosted: Monday October 15 2018, 12:53pm\nPhotograph: Courtesy LinkNYC\nWhen the sleek, black LinkNYC kiosks began popping up around New York in 2016, it felt sort of like the opening scene of 2001: A Space Odyssey. Technologically advanced monoliths from the future had suddenly materialized to drag us all into the future. Two years later, the internet-connected sidewalk kiosks\xe2\x80\x94which offer free Wi-Fi, free calling and USB ports to charge devices\xe2\x80\x94can boast\xc2\xa0more than 5 million registered Wi-Fi users who log an average of 20 million free sessions a week. Additionally, 500,000 phone calls are made on the kiosks every month.\nSo can we look forward to a sunny future where we can all cancel our private internet plans and log onto a free public network that blankets the city?\xc2\xa0Unfortunately, no. \xe2\x80\x9cLinkNYC kiosks are primarily designed for commercial corridors,\xe2\x80\x9d explains Kate Blumm, Assistant Commissioner at the NYC Department of Information Technology. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just one piece of the mayor\xe2\x80\x99s larger plan to bring affordable high-speed internet to every New Yorker by 2025.\xe2\x80\x9d Additionally, the 1,700 kiosks that have been installed across the five boroughs (of a planned 7,500) only offer a Wi-Fi range of about 150 feet.\nWhen NYC originally conceptualized the project that eventually became LinkNYC, it was looking for a modern replacement for the city\xe2\x80\x99s aging payphone infrastructure. The winning proposal, from CityBridge, envisioned futuristic metal totems spread out across all five boroughs with giant, high-res screens on either side. Advertisements shown on the screens would then cover the cost of the kiosks themselves, and the city would be gifted with free, fast Wi-Fi infrastructure. To date, however, some of the most compelling uses of the kiosks have come from those screens rather than the Wi-Fi.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe were surprised by how many people have been using them to make calls when everyone has cell phone, but a big part of the kiosks has been the content we display on the screens,\xe2\x80\x9d says Jennifer Hensley, the president of Link. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re able to provided curated content to help people make the most of their city through partnerships with local government and cultural institutions.\xe2\x80\x9d That\xe2\x80\x99s ranged from a recent initiative where New Yorkers could literally register to vote using the kiosks to information on good restaurants to hit up in the area, fun facts about the city and details on upcoming local events that those passing by might want to attend.\nOne of the criticisms of the kiosks from privacy advocates has been the inclusion of two cameras above the displays (along with a third camera above the tablet which could possibly be used for video calling in the future). Hensley insists, however, that the cameras above the New York devices are primarily for monitoring the structures themselves. \xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re expensive pieces of hardware out on the streets so we want to make sure they\xe2\x80\x99re safe,\xe2\x80\x9d she says.\nAlong with the addition of thousands of more kiosks in the coming years, Hensley predicts that the devices will play a large part in coming years with helping New Yorkers have all the information they need to be counted in the 2020 census. However, by that time, Link will be helping more than just New Yorkers. The company has plans to expand into Newark this\xc2\xa0week\xc2\xa0and will soon spread to Philadelphia by the end of the year.\nAdvertising\nAdvertising\nShare\nTweet\nGuest blogger\nBy Will Gleason. Oct. 16, 2018. (Courtesy: City of Newark)\nBy Karen Yi | NJ Advance Media for NJ.com\nNew digital kiosks with 55-inch screens have\xc2\xa0sprouted across the city of Newark\xc2\xa0that will allow passers-by to make free phone calls, connect to public Wifi or charge their mobile devices.Newark is the first in New Jersey to\xc2\xa0launch the LinkNWK sidewalk\xc2\xa0kiosks\xc2\xa0created by\xc2\xa0Intersection, a New York-based technology company. New York City was the first to roll out the technology in 2016 and Philadelphia will install the kiosks later this fall.\nOn Tuesday, officials debuted\xc2\xa0the newly-installed\xc2\xa0kiosks across from the\xc2\xa0Prudential Center on Broad Street. A\xc2\xa0total of 45 kiosks will be in operation in the city -- with at least one in every ward. So far, two are up and running."Newark is once again defining itself to the state, nation, and world as a cutting-edge, high-tech city," Mayor Ras Baraka said. "These kiosks will enable residents and visitors alike to gain immediate information about Newark, ranging from upcoming cultural events to emergency service response."The kiosks, which Intersection installed at no cost to the city, display information on city services, fun facts about Newark, upcoming events and advertisements.The ad revenue will go to the company and be shared with the city as well.Representatives at\xc2\xa0Intersection said this time, the kiosks will not allow internet browsing. When the devices were first installed in New York City people used the kiosks to watch pornography, according to reports at the time.\nLinkNWK kiosk on Broad Street. Oct. 16, 2018. (Courtesy: City of Newark)\nThe company has not announced plans to install kiosks in any other New Jersey cities.The Newark kiosks will be the first to roll out with a Wifi app that allows users to connect to the LinkNWK network and pull up a map to find the nearest kiosk.\nNJIT has also partnered with Intersection\xc2\xa0to find creative ways of using the devices to benefit the community."Newark is a rising star in the tech economy, and we are proud that LinkNWK will only add to this momentum," said Jen Hensley, President of Link at Intersection.A minority investor in Intersection is Sidewalk Labs, which was created by Alphabet, the parent company of Google. Karen Yi may be reached at\xc2\xa0kyi@njadvancemedia.com. Follow her\xc2\xa0on Twitter at\xc2\xa0@karen_yi\xc2\xa0or on\xc2\xa0Facebook.\nView Comments\nFooter Navigation\nDisclaimer\nRegistration on or use of this site constitutes acceptance of our User Agreement and Privacy Policy\n\xc2\xa9 2019 New Jersey On-Line LLC. Community Rules apply to all content you upload or otherwise submit to this site.\nAd Choices', b"New York\xe2\x80\x99s wi-fi kiosks display new Jackie Robinson photos | StateScoop\nSubscribe\nAbout\nRSS\nBrought to you by\nSpecial Reports\nState\nCity\nCounty & Local\nWatch\nListen\nAttend\nContent Studio\nNew York's digital information kiosks displaying newly published Jackie Robinson photos\nJackie Robinson, 1953 (Kenneith Eide / Museum of the City of New York)\nShare\nWritten by Benjamin Freed\nFeb 5, 2019 | STATESCOOP\nThe 1,700 digital information kiosks scattered around New York City are being used this month to promote a new museum exhibit celebrating the 100th anniversary of the birth of Jackie Robinson.\nThe city\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Information Technology and Telecommunications, which operates the LinkNYC kiosks, is partnering with the Museum of the City of New York to display previously unpublished photographs of\xc2\xa0Robinson, who broke Major League Baseball\xe2\x80\x99s racial barrier when he joined the Brooklyn Dodgers in 1948.\nNew York started installing the kiosks in 2016, placing them on the locations of antiquated phone booths. The kiosks nominally serve as public Wi-Fi hotspots, USB charging stations, free-to-use telephones and touchscreen directories of city services. Last April, DoITT added real-time bus schedules\xc2\xa0to the kiosks\xe2\x80\x99 displays, and is now using them to showcase the photography exhibition.\nThe exhibit, \xe2\x80\x9cIn the Dugout with Jackie Robinson: An Intimate Portrait of a Baseball Legend,\xe2\x80\x9d includes 32 photographs of Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s 10-year MLB career and personal life. The pictures were originally shot for Look magazine by photographers Kenneth Eide and Frank Bauman, but never published. The scenes include Robinson on and off the field at Ebbets Field, in the Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 clubhouse and at home with his wife, Rachel.\nJackie and Rachel Robinson with their three-year-old son, Jackie Jr., at home in Brooklyn, 1949. (Frank Bauman / Museum of the City of New York)\nWhile the full exhibit, which also includes memorabilia and the Robinson family\xe2\x80\x99s home movies, is on display at the Museum of the City of New York through Sept. 15, the LinkNYC kiosks will be rotating through the photos until Feb. 28, as part of the city\xe2\x80\x99s commemoration of Black History Month. A museum dedicated to Robinson, who died in 1972, is scheduled to open in December.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat better way to celebrate Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s rich legacy, life and career in New York in a way that everyone walking down the street can enjoy,\xe2\x80\x9d Samir Saini, New York\xe2\x80\x99s chief information officer, said in a press release.\n-In this Story-\nJackie Robinson, LinkNYC\nRelated news\nCity\nLos Angeles city controller updates online property map to boost housing, economy\nby Colin Wood \xe2\x80\xa2 2 days ago\nCity\n'Bootcamp' program aims to boost New York City's cybersecurity workforce\nby Benjamin Freed \xe2\x80\xa2 2 days ago\nCity\nDetroit kicks off Ford-backed transportation challenge\nby Ryan Johnston \xe2\x80\xa2 2 days ago\nAd Specs\nSponsor\nRSS\nPrivacy Policy\n\xc2\xa9 2019 Scoop News Group\n|\nAll Rights Reserved\nSearch for:\nThe latest state and local government tech news, delivered straight to your inbox.\nSign up for our daily newsletter.\nPrivacy Policy\nWe use cookies to provide you with the best experience across all Scoop News Group websites.
